# Changelog

All notable changes to this project will be documented in this file.

The format is based on [Keep a Changelog](https://keepachangelog.com/en/1.1.0/).

## [Unreleased]

### Added
- **Boot-time bootstrap for service mode (A1).** The server now warms its background caches/watchers at process start instead of waiting for the first dashboard visit: the project-scan cache, the `gitStatusCache`/`efficiencyGradeCache`/`githubActivityCache` enqueue (via a new shared `src/lib/projectCacheEnqueue.ts`, extracted from `/api/projects` so both call sites share one enqueue rule), `manualStepsWatcher`, `mcpConfigWatcher`, `mcpHealthCache` (mirrors `GET /api/mcp-health`'s enqueue against the merged user-scope MCP server list), and a `claudeStatus` prime — plus a `probeInitStatus()` DB-readiness probe (never bypassing the retry/classification state machine). New `src/lib/bootstrap.ts` (`runBootstrap`, `shouldBootstrap`) is wired into the existing root `instrumentation.ts` → `instrumentation-node.ts` boot path (alongside the pre-existing dispatcher/ingest-watcher startup), guarded by a `globalThis` idempotency flag so a dev/HMR re-fire of `register()` can't double-run it. **Gating:** default **on** when `NODE_ENV === "production"`; opt-in in dev via a new **`MINDER_BOOTSTRAP=1`** env var (a full project scan on every `next dev` restart would be hostile to the edit loop); `MINDER_BOOTSTRAP=0` disables it everywhere. Always skipped in demo mode (`MINDER_DEMO=1` or the `demoMode` flag). `skillUpdateCache` was deliberately **not** wired — unlike the other three singletons it has no standalone idempotent starter; it's only enqueued from inside the `/api/agents`/`/api/skills` catalog-build query modules, and replicating that at boot would mean duplicating the full indexer walk to warm a 24-hour-TTL cache. Each subsystem logs one line and is independently try/caught, so one failure (e.g. an unreadable devRoot) never blocks the others. Covered by `tests/bootstrap.test.ts` (pure gating precedence, demo-mode skip, per-subsystem call counts, idempotency across repeated `runBootstrap()` calls, and failure isolation).

### Fixed
- **Interface text now meets WCAG AA contrast on the dark theme.** The neutral text ramp was too dark against the deep-steel surfaces: `--text-muted` (`--text-3`, used in ~995 places — `.page-sub`, `.li-sub`/`.li-meta`, `.stat-card` labels/deltas, breadcrumbs, card subtitles, row descriptions, and most secondary metadata) sat at only **~2.3:1**, roughly half the 4.5:1 AA threshold for normal text — the "light gray text on black" that was hard to read. The four `--text-*` tokens in `globals.css` were re-tuned by luminance (not eyeballed OKLCH lightness) to clear AA while preserving the four-tier hierarchy: `--text-primary` .93 (unchanged, ~16:1 AAA), `--text-secondary` .62→**.72** (~7:1), `--text-muted` .42→**.62** (5.1–5.7:1, AA), `--text-disabled` .30→**.50** (3.1–3.4:1 — reserved for decorative/disabled/status use only). Readable metadata that had been using the faint `--text-4` tier (the dashboard period subtext, DB last-error line, per-project last-activity timestamps, and the Claude-status "last checked" note) was reclassified to `--text-3` so it clears AA — a distinct neutral tier *below* muted can't be AA on light card surfaces, so `--text-4` is now documented as non-text-only. `--status-archived-text` was lifted to match muted. Separately, the colored badge/tag text (`.tag.*`, `.nav-item .badge`) sat at 3.6–4.5:1 on its same-hue tint; the wash was lowered 12–14%→**10%** (darker background raises same-hue contrast) and the three darkest color tokens brightened — `--info` .68→.72, `--status-error-text` (`--danger`) .65→.72, `--purple` .68→.73 — so all tag variants now clear 4.5:1. Brand tokens `--accent` (amber) and `--good` (green) were left unchanged. Also fixed a pre-existing failure: the top-bar notification `.badge-dot` rendered white count text on `--danger` (3.5:1, and worse once `--danger` brightened); it now uses the darker `--destructive` fill (`#fff` at 5.3:1). No component markup changed — the fix is entirely in the design tokens, so all ~1400 token references update at once.
- **Sidebar navigation and the workflow-launcher chips are no longer faint.** AA is a floor, not a comfort target, and the always-on nav chrome (small, uppercase, low-weight) still read as too dim at the minimum. Navigation is now lifted toward full strength: `.nav-item` labels use `--text` (primary) instead of `--text-2`; nav-group section headers use `--text-2` (hover/active → `--text`); `.nav-section-label` and the project-switcher scope label step up from `--text-4`/`--text-3` to `--text-3`/`--text-2`; and the stacked `opacity` dimming on nav icons (`.85→1`) and group chevrons (`.6→.85`) was removed. The "Quick Launch" launcher chips now render their label at `--text-primary` (hover feedback moved to a background tint) and the strip heading at `--text-secondary`.
- **`agent-view` readable text now meets WCAG AA (closes #277).** The experimental agent-view subsystem still used the `--text-4` tier (`~3:1`) for real body text — peek-panel labels/timestamps/"Loading…", tree-view node labels and "depth N" meta, agent-card worktree/model/age text, and board empty-states. Those usages were reclassified to `--text-3` (`5.1–5.6:1`, AA), matching the #276 rule that `--text-4` is decorative/disabled/status-only. The **`AgentCard` metadata uses `--text-2`** rather than `--text-3`, because the card's root background is *status-tinted* (`waiting`→amber `#451a03`, `completed`→green `#052e16`) where `--text-3` measures only ~4.1:1 — `--text-2` clears 4.5:1 on every status background (6.0–7.6:1). The intentional de-emphasized **status color maps** (`idle`/`stopped`/`reconnecting`/`connecting` and the toolbar stale-state fallback) and the genuinely-disabled dev-server button were deliberately left on `--text-4`. The dead `,#555` CSS-var fallbacks were updated to a matching `#8a8c8f` at the same time. Verified live via canvas pixel readback.
- **Sidebar nav labels are now near-white.** `--text-primary` (OKLCH L=0.93) is a light gray, not white, so even at 16:1 the always-on menu still read soft. Introduced two dedicated navigation tokens — `--nav-text` (`oklch(0.985 …)`, ~18–20:1 near-white) for nav destinations, and `--nav-section` (`oklch(0.82 …)`, ~11:1) for uppercase group/section headers — and pointed `.nav-item`, `.nav-group-head` (hover/active → `--nav-text`), and `.nav-section-label` at them. Nav destinations now render at ~`rgb(249,250,251)` and section headers at ~`rgb(194,196,199)`, both AAA and visibly white/bright rather than gray.

## [1.2.0] - 2026-07-15

### Fixed
- **Demo mode no longer shows empty Hot Files / Errors / Patterns tabs (demo-mode fast-follow).** Those three per-project tabs read real `~/.claude` session JSONL keyed on the synthetic `C:\dev\<slug>` demo path, which has no fixtures, so they rendered blank in demo mode. `ProjectData` gains a payload-borne **`demo?: boolean`** marker (set only by the `src/lib/demo/` fixtures, so it's robust to *both* activation paths — the `MINDER_DEMO=1` env var and the `demoMode` flag — where reading the client-side flag alone would miss the env toggle), and `ProjectDetail` hides the three tabs for demo projects (`showSessionAnalysisTabs = hasSessions && !isDemoProject`). A deep link that targets a hidden session-analysis tab (`?tab=hot-files|errors|patterns` from a bookmark, a shared URL, or a stale query string after enabling demo mode) now falls back to Overview, and the three content branches are gated on `showSessionAnalysisTabs` too, so the empty panel can't render regardless of how `activeTab` was seeded. This mirrors how `SessionDetailView` suppresses index-only tabs for `demo-…` sessions. **Efficiency stays** — its route already carries a demo guard and renders a structured report. No leak and no write was ever involved (the tabs were simply empty). Covered by a new `tests/demoProjects.test.ts` case asserting `demo: true` on every fixture.
- **Subagent transcript files (`<session>/subagents/agent-*.jsonl`) now ingest correctly.** Newer Claude Code writes subagent transcripts to separate per-agent JSONL files instead of inlining sidechain entries in the parent session file. These files are sidechain-only (zero primary turns), which broke ingest three ways: (1) the tail-append path's primary-filtered `SUM` aggregates evaluated to `NULL` over zero rows and violated `sessions.user_turn_count NOT NULL` — rolling back the transaction, never advancing the byte cursor, and retry-failing on every append (`[ingest-watcher] reconcile … failed: NOT NULL constraint failed` log spam); (2) the watcher attributed them to a literal `subagents` project (it derived the project from the file's immediate parent directory instead of the first segment under the watch root); (3) the sweep never discovered them, so its prune pass deleted any session row a watcher event had created. Aggregates are now `COALESCE`d, project attribution uses the watch-root-relative first segment, the sweep walks `<project>/<session-id>/subagents/*.jsonl` (registering them as live), session time bounds fall back to sidechain rows, and a `project_dir_name` mismatch forces a full-replace so previously mispinned rows self-heal. Sidechain-only session rows are excluded from the sessions browser (`turn_count > 0`) — they exist so subagent token spend reaches the usage rollups, not as browsable sessions.
- **Worker-mode ingest no longer self-destructs on a slow initial reconcile.** The ingest worker acked `started` only after its initial reconcile completed; after a `DERIVED_VERSION` bump that's a full corpus re-parse (minutes), guaranteed to blow the host's 60 s start timeout — whose fallback then hard-`terminate()`d the healthy worker mid-SQLite-write (a documented better-sqlite3 corruption vector, the likely source of the FTS5 `prompts_fts` corruption → quarantine → full rebuild cascade on boot) and redid the whole reconcile in-process. The watcher now supports `deferInitialReconcile` (worker mode passes it): `started` acks as soon as the watcher is armed, the initial reconcile runs in the background behind an in-flight flag (per-file reconciles and sweep ticks reschedule instead of racing it), and completion is reported to the host as an `initial-reconcile` message (logged).
- **`stopWorker` now stops gracefully before terminating.** It posts `stop` and gives a post-`ready` worker up to 5 s to exit cleanly between transactions before falling back to `terminate()` — hard-killing a worker thread mid-better-sqlite3-write can corrupt the database. Workers that never reached `ready` (stuck/broken, not running ingest) are still terminated immediately.
- **Watcher-driven reconciles now refresh `category_costs`.** The per-file watcher path refreshed only `daily_costs` after a live append, dropping the reconcile's `affectedCategoryTuples`; because the reconcile advances the file's cursor, the sweep saw the file as unchanged and never backfilled, so the `/api/usage` by-category breakdown went stale for live-appended spend (including the newly-ingested subagent transcripts) until a forced full re-parse. The watcher now refreshes both rollups, matching `reconcileAllSessions`.
- **OTEL ingest routes no longer 500 with `SQLITE_BUSY` during background reconciles.** `otelIngest` write transactions (single log/metric and batch paths) now retry twice with a short async backoff when the ingest watcher's reconcile holds the WAL writer lock past the 5 s `busy_timeout`.

### Changed
- **`src/middleware.ts` → `src/proxy.ts` (Next.js 16 convention).** The S1 Host/Origin API-protection layer is unchanged in behavior; the file and exported function follow Next 16's renamed `proxy` file convention, silencing the boot-time deprecation warning. Docs updated (`docs/help/security.md`).
- **Internal: split oversized `types.ts` / `ingest.ts` into domain modules (facade-preserving).** `src/lib/types.ts` (~1560 lines) is sliced into cohesive domain modules under `src/lib/types/` (`project`, `session`, `board`, `ops`, `config`, `claudeConfig`, `lint`, `stats`, `template`, etc.) with `src/lib/types/index.ts` as a barrel that `export *`s every module, so the ~190 files importing `@/lib/types` are unchanged. Pure, module-state-free helpers in `src/lib/db/ingest.ts` (`extractFileOp`/`extractAgentName`/`extractSkillName`/`truncateText`/`readTailToLastNewline` → `ingest/parseHelpers.ts`; `safeExtractPrs`/`safeExtractTickets`/`mergePrLinks`/`mergeTicketLinks` → `ingest/merge.ts`) are extracted into sibling modules and re-imported; the public export surface of `@/lib/db/ingest` is unchanged. The cross-backend post-processing that could be shared between the SQLite and file-parse usage paths was already factored into shared helpers (`toLocalDateStr`, `groupByBinary`, `parseStoredArgs`); the remaining per-function divergences are intentional and left in place. No user-facing behavior change.
- **RSC server-prefetch, Server Actions, and SSE live-updates are now enabled by default (were opt-in); bespoke pollers migrated to TanStack Query / the SSE bus.** The `rscHydration`, `serverActions`, and `liveEvents` feature flags — the shipped-but-dormant PR #237–#243 architecture — now default **on** (meta `defaultOn: true` and every call site reads `getFlag(..., key)` with no explicit `false`, so the Settings toggle and the runtime gate agree). Read-heavy pages now server-prefetch and hydrate, the two live writes route through Server Actions, and the client opens the single `/api/events` SSE stream by default; each flag can still be toggled **off** in **Settings**, which falls back to the intact client fetch-on-mount / POST-route / timer-poll paths. Alongside, seven hand-rolled `setInterval`+`fetch` pollers were migrated to `useQuery` with a matching `refetchInterval` and `refetchIntervalInBackground: false` so a backgrounded tab no longer polls: `useEfficiencyGrades`, `StatusDashboard` (3s), `DevServerControl` (2s, conditional), `SettingsPage` DB-health (15s), `BackgroundActivityBrowser` (15s); `useGitDirtyStatus` / `useGithubActivity` already ride the SSE bus by default and gained tab-visibility guards on their polling fallback. The two redundant 60s claude-status pollers (`ClaudeStatusBanner` + `ClaudeStatusListener`) are consolidated into a single `ClaudeStatusProvider` (one `useQuery` against a new combined `GET /api/claude-status/live` endpoint that returns snapshot + change events in one response) that feeds both the banner and the change-toast listener — one request instead of two.

### Added
- **Live MCP server health strip (spike).** The top bar now shows a compact row of health dots — one per configured MCP server across every user-scope source (managed policy, `~/.claude/settings.json`, `~/.claude.json`, Claude Desktop, and plugins, via the shared `getUserConfig` reader) — so you can see at a glance whether your connected MCP servers are actually reachable, not just configured. Health means different things per transport, and the UI is honest about it: **http/sse** servers get a real reachability probe (any HTTP response — even a `401`/`405` — proves the server is *listening*, so it's **up**; only a connection failure or timeout is **down**; `fetch` resolves on response headers and the stream is cancelled, so an SSE endpoint that holds its body open still reads up quickly), while **stdio** servers can't be health-checked without spawning them, so the signal is launchability — the command resolves on PATH (**up**, tooltip says "launchable — not probed") vs missing (**down**). Disabled or unknown-transport servers render a neutral dot. Backed by a pure, unit-tested probe layer (`src/lib/mcpHealth.ts` — `probeMcpServer` + a Windows-PATHEXT-aware `resolveCommandOnPath`) and a background-poller cache (`src/lib/mcpHealthCache.ts`) that mirrors `githubActivityCache` exactly (queue, `seen` dedupe, `generation`-guarded `dispose()`, batched `processQueue`, 5-min TTL, `get`/`getAll`/`pending`/`total`). New **`GET /api/mcp-health`** both gates (on a new **default-on `mcpHealth`** feature flag) and enqueues, since the strip is a single global surface with no per-project fan-out; the route filters its response to the currently-configured server names (a removed server drops off immediately instead of lingering to TTL), and the cache keys each verdict by a config **signature** (transport/command/args/url/disabled) so a server that repoints under the same name re-probes rather than showing a stale dot; the `McpHealthIndicator` client component self-gates (renders nothing when the flag is off or before the first probe lands) and polls faster (2s) while probes are in flight, then settles to 15s. Covered by `tests/mcpHealth.test.ts` (PATH resolution incl. PATHEXT and explicit paths; http/sse up/down/timeout classification; stdio launchable/missing; disabled/unknown → neutral); the `mcpHealth` flag is picked up by the existing key/meta exhaustiveness checks in `tests/featureFlags.test.ts`. First of four capabilities ported from the `agentic-os-dashboard` review.
- **MCP health strip — popover, help doc, and instant-drop watcher (follow-ups).** The strip is now a **click-through popover**: clicking the dots opens a panel listing every server (status, `transport` + `source` chips, probe detail, and an `up · down · unknown` footer), sorted problems-first, with a `?` that opens the new help doc. `source` was added to `McpHealth` and threaded through the probe/cache so two same-name servers from different sources are visually disambiguated. A new **`docs/help/mcp-health.md`** (+ `public/help` mirror, slug wired into `help-mapping.ts` + `HelpPanel`) documents the per-transport semantics. And a new **`src/lib/mcpConfigWatcher.ts`** watches `~/.claude.json` + `~/.claude/settings.json` and invalidates the shared user-config cache **only when the `mcpServers` slice actually changes** (a signature guard — `~/.claude.json` is rewritten constantly by Claude Code, so a naive watch would thrash the cache and force the expensive multi-source re-read every poll), so a server removed by hand-editing config now drops from the strip within seconds instead of at the 5-min TTL. Covered by `tests/mcpConfigWatcher.test.ts` (the signature ignores unrelated runtime-state fields and key-order, but changes on add/remove/redefine).
- **MCP health — opt-in real stdio handshake.** A new **default-off `mcpHealthStdioProbe`** feature flag upgrades stdio servers from the PATH-launchability check to a genuine health probe: `src/lib/mcpStdioProbe.ts` briefly **spawns the server** and performs an MCP `initialize` JSON-RPC round-trip — a valid `result` is **up** (`probeKind: "handshake"`, detail `initialize ok — <serverInfo.name>`), a JSON-RPC error / early exit / spawn-ENOENT / timeout is **down**. It's off by default because spawning the real server may connect to actual backends. Secrets are handled carefully: a stdio server usually needs its `env` (credentials) to start, and Minder never *retains* env values, so the probe reads them **transiently** from the source config file, passes them straight to the spawned child, and lets them fall out of scope — they never reach the health verdict, cache, or logs. `probeMcpServer` migrated to an options object (`{ env, platform, stdioHandshake, … }`); the cache threads the flag and re-probes on toggle. Covered by `tests/mcpStdioProbe.test.ts` (valid/error/exit/ENOENT/timeout/no-command, and non-JSON log lines ignored) + a routing case in `tests/mcpHealth.test.ts`. Completes the four `agentic-os-dashboard` port follow-ups.
- **Persistent burn HUD in the top bar (agentic-os-dashboard port #2).** The top bar now shows a compact **`BURN`** chip that always surfaces how hard you're burning against your Claude rate limits — the more-utilized of your **5h/7d** rolling windows (colour-coded green/amber/red) plus a projected **`cap ~3:40 PM`** when you're on track to hit 100% before that window resets — so you can pace a long session without opening Settings. Clicking opens a popover with all three windows (5h / 7d / overage), each with its utilization bar, reset countdown, and a schedule-aware `~N% projected` end-of-window estimate; the 7d projection is scaled by the configured schedule (you won't burn 24/7) while 5h and the cap-time use the raw linear rate. The projection reads the **same authoritative `anthropic-ratelimit-unified-*` headers** the `/settings` burndown chart uses (via `loadQuota`/`useQuota`) rather than re-deriving from indexed usage turns — the header already reflects real consumption across every Claude client on the account, so the HUD can't drift from the real limit. The projection math is extracted into a pure, unit-tested `src/lib/quotaProjection.ts` (`computeProjectedUtilization` / `computeCapTimeMs` / `computeBurnHeadline` / `formatCountdown`), and `QuotaBurndownChart` is refactored to consume it (killing the prior duplication). Gated behind a new **default-on `burnHud`** feature flag (`useBurnHudEnabled`); the `QuotaHud` client component additionally **self-hides** whenever there's nothing to show — flag off, no valid Claude OAuth credentials, probe failed, or the first fetch hasn't resolved (no empty-state flash). New `docs/help/burn-hud.md` (+ `public/help` mirror; slug wired into `help-mapping.ts` + `HelpPanel`). Covered by `tests/quotaProjection.test.ts` (linear extrapolation, 200% clamp, schedule scaling of 7d vs continuous 5h, bogus/zero-reset → null, cap-time before/at/after reset, already-capped, worst-window + soonest-cap headline selection, and countdown formatting); the `burnHud` flag is picked up by the existing exhaustiveness checks in `tests/featureFlags.test.ts`. Second of four capabilities ported from the `agentic-os-dashboard` review.
- **Demo mode — synthetic data across the whole dashboard (agentic-os-dashboard port #3).** A new toggle fills **every** read surface with deterministic, realistic fixtures so Minder looks alive on a machine with no real `~/.claude` history or `C:\dev` project tree — for first-run tours, marketing screenshots, and live demos. Turned on two ways (either wins): the **`MINDER_DEMO=1` env var** (forces on with no persisted config write — the CI/screenshot switch, mirroring the `MINDER_USE_DB` idiom) or a new **default-off `demoMode` feature flag** (an in-app **Settings** toggle for live demos). Fixtures live in `src/lib/demo/` (`projects`, `sessions`, `usage`, `catalogs`, `activity`) and are **deterministic but anchored to "now"** — every timestamp is a fixed offset from a `nowMs` captured at request time, so relative times ("2h ago", "today") stay fresh across runs while the structure is byte-stable (reproducible screenshots). The guards inject at the data-source seams **above** the DB/file branch (so a demo run on a machine with no SQLite index can't throw `DbUnavailableError`, and the default-on `MINDER_USE_DB` can't skip them): one guard atop **`scanAllProjects()`** returns a synthetic `ProjectData[]` — which, because board/insights/manual-steps/ops/worktrees all ride on `ProjectData` from the scan cache, lights up projects, project detail, board, insights, manual-steps, ops, and stats in a single seam; early-returns in the **`data/index.ts` façade** (`getSessionsList`, `getSessionDetail`, `getUsage`, `getClaudeUsage`, `getAgentUsage`, `getSkillUsage`, `searchSessions`) cover sessions and the full usage/cost analytics; and the **catalog loaders** (`loadAgentsResponse`/`loadSkillsResponse`) plus the four **activity-strip routes** (`/api/github-activity`, `/api/git-status`, `/api/mcp-health`, `/api/integrations/quota`) light up the agents/skills catalogs, the GitHub/CI strip, git dirty counts, MCP health dots, and the burn HUD. The synthetic portfolio is 8 projects across active/paused/archived, ~17 sessions, ~$138 of usage with by-model/by-category/by-day breakdowns, 6 agents, 5 skills, and matching activity. Read-only: no files are written and no real projects, sessions, or credentials are touched. New `docs/help/demo-mode.md` (+ `public/help` mirror; slug wired into `help-mapping.ts` + `HelpPanel`); `MINDER_DEMO` documented in `CLAUDE.md`. Covered by `tests/demoMode.test.ts` (env-vs-flag precedence, default-off), `tests/demoProjects.test.ts` (determinism, now-anchoring, required-`ProjectData`-core, panel coverage), and `tests/demoFixtures.test.ts` (every generator deterministic + non-trivial, unknown-session fallback, quota configured, git dirty counts). Third of four capabilities ported from the `agentic-os-dashboard` review.
- **One-click workflow launcher chips (agentic-os-dashboard port #4 — final).** A thin launcher that turns a curated workflow into a single click — a gentler on-ramp than the full Swarm composer. Each chip dispatches **one** dispatcher task (`POST /api/tasks`) scoped to a project, so the existing `claude -p` pipeline runs it in that project's directory. Two placements, both gated by a new **default-on `workflowLauncher`** feature flag: a **per-project "Quick Launch" strip** on `/project/[slug]` (between the header and the tabs — chips dispatch immediately against that project) and a **global row under the top bar** on every other page (a chip click first opens a **project picker**, since a task must run *somewhere*; the global row is hidden on the project detail route so the two strips never double up). Chips come from two sources shown side by side: the curated **`LAUNCHER_WORKFLOWS`** gallery (🔍 Review diff · 🧪 Test & fix · 🩺 Typecheck & lint · 📝 Update CHANGELOG · 🧹 Tidy TODO.md · 📦 Dependency audit — each prompt written self-contained and stating its own blast radius, e.g. "do not modify files" / "only edit CHANGELOG.md"), and the user's **user-invocable skills** (pulled from `/api/skills`, filtered to `userInvocable && !disabled`, capped, dispatching the bare `/name` invocation). A successful launch shows a toast with a **View in Tasks** link; **demo mode is read-only** (a click returns a `409` and toasts "Read-only in demo mode"). **Enabler:** `validateCreateTask` previously *dropped* `metadata`, so a `POST /api/tasks` always ran in the server's cwd — it now threads a validated `metadata` object through (type-checking `metadata.projectPath` / `metadata.worktreePath`, the keys the spawner's `taskCwd` reads), which is what lets a launched task target the chosen project. `POST /api/tasks` also gains the shared `demoWriteBlock()` guard. Pure data + builders live in `src/lib/launchers/definitions.ts` (`LAUNCHER_WORKFLOWS`, `buildWorkflowDispatch`, `buildSkillDispatch`, `selectSkillChips`); UI in `src/components/LauncherChips.tsx` + `GlobalLauncherRow.tsx`; new `useWorkflowLauncherEnabled()` hook. New `docs/help/workflow-launcher.md` (+ `public/help` mirror; slug wired into `help-mapping.ts` + `HelpPanel`). Covered by `tests/launchers.test.ts` (curated-gallery integrity, dispatch builders, skill-chip selection/cap/sort) and new `metadata` pass-through/rejection cases in `tests/tasksValidation.test.ts`; the `workflowLauncher` flag is picked up by the existing exhaustiveness checks in `tests/featureFlags.test.ts`. **Completes the four `agentic-os-dashboard` ports.**
- **Cost-per-project report + per-project Costs tab, sliced by six time periods.** A new **`/costs`** dashboard (sidebar → Review → "Cost report", hover-prefetched) ranks **every** project by Claude Code spend for a single active period — where the Home card shows only the top 6 and the Usage page's By-Project list caps at 12, this is the full portfolio in a sortable table (Project · Cost · Share · Tokens · Turns) with a name filter and a totals row; each scanned-project row links to that project's new **Costs** tab. That tab (on `/project/[slug]`, shown when the project has Claude sessions) shows the project's headline cost/tokens/turns/sessions plus by-model and by-category breakdowns for the selected period. Both surfaces reuse the existing `GET /api/usage?period=&project=` endpoint (no new route). **Two new periods — rolling `90d` and `1y` (365d) — were added to the canonical `VALID_PERIODS`** (with `quarter`/`year`/`365d` aliases and `getPeriodStart` cutoffs), so the Cost report and the per-project tab offer **Today / 7d / 30d / 90d / 1y / All** (a `COST_PERIODS` subset that drops `24h`); the two new windows also now appear on the Usage dashboard and the agent/skill detail toggles (the share-image `periodLabel` map was extended to match — and now falls back to the raw period string instead of rendering `undefined` for any unmapped value, closing a pre-existing `24h` gap too). To join a scanned project to its usage aggregates, `ProjectData` gains a precomputed **`usageSlug`** field — the usage module keys turns on a slug derived from the encoded `~/.claude/projects/` dir (`dev-project-minder`), which differs from the filesystem-basename route slug (`project-minder`); the scanner now derives it server-side via the same `encodePath → canonicalizeDirName → toSlug` pipeline the parser uses, so the Costs tab and the report's row-links resolve correctly instead of silently showing `$0`. New `docs/help/cost-report.md` (+ `public/help` mirror); route + `costs` tab wired into `help-mapping.ts`. Covered by new `tests/usageSlugBridge.test.ts` (path→usage-slug derivation incl. drive-case, non-alphanumeric, and worktree-suffix stripping) and new `90d`/`1y`/alias + `DETAIL_PERIODS` cases in `tests/usagePeriod.test.ts`.
- **Board MCP write-bridge + task bridge (Portfolio Command Deck — Phase 2).** A running Claude Code session can now push work into a project's canonical `BOARD.md` — and bridge it into the task dispatcher — without leaving the terminal. **Four new MCP tools** (`src/lib/mcp/tools/board.ts`, registered in `server.ts`): `board_create_issue` (under an epic or the Inbox, with optional `status`/`priority`/`labels` and `sessionId`/`worktree` provenance), `board_log_finding` (a `(finding) …` Inbox row at status `triage`), `board_postpone` (snooze → `backlog`, or any explicit status), and `board_promote_to_task` (bridge an issue into a `~/.minder/tasks.db` task, returning `{ taskId, board }`). They call the Phase 1 writer / promote lib directly (no HTTP loopback), resolve `slug → parent path` via `findProjectPathBySlug` (so a worktree path can't fragment the board), and `invalidateCache()` after each write; out-of-enum `status`/`priority` is rejected at the JSON-RPC boundary via new `BoardStatusSchema`/`BoardPrioritySchema`, and an unknown slug or stale issue id surfaces as an `isError` result. The same capability is exposed in the UI: a new **`promoteToTask` action on `POST /api/board/[slug]`** and a **"Promote to task" row action on the Board tab** (shows `→ task #N` once bridged), both backed by a new **`src/lib/tasks/boardDelegation.ts`** (`promoteBoardIssueToTask`) that stamps board provenance (`sourceType: "board-issue"`, `boardIssueId`, `projectSlug`) into the `delegated-todo` task's metadata. The lifecycle is **two-way and best-effort**: promoting flips the issue to `doing`, and the dispatcher's completion hook (`onTaskCompleteSyncBoard`) flips it to `done` when the task finishes (a missing/edited issue never fails the task). Covered by `tests/mcpBoardTools.test.ts` (tool→lib wiring + error surfacing) and `tests/boardDelegation.test.ts`. Docs: `docs/help/mcp-server.md` (board write-tools table) and `docs/help/board.md` ("Promote to task" + "Agent write-bridge (MCP)") updated (+ `public/help` mirrors).
- **GitHub activity surface (Portfolio Command Deck — Phase 4).** Each project now surfaces the three things that usually make you switch to a GitHub tab — **open PRs**, **CI pass/fail on the default branch**, and **how long ago the last push was** — directly on the dashboard card and the project detail page. A new **`githubActivityCache`** (`src/lib/githubActivityCache.ts`) mirrors the proven `gitStatusCache` pipeline exactly: a `globalThis` singleton with a queue, `seen` dedupe, `generation`-based `dispose()` race protection, batched `processQueue` (gentler `BATCH_SIZE`/`BATCH_DELAY` since each repo costs up to three `gh` round-trips), a 5-min TTL, and `get`/`getAll`/`pending`/`total` accessors. It shells out to the user's **local authenticated `gh` CLI** (`gh pr list` / `gh run list` / `gh repo view`) and is **fully defensive**: a missing/unauthenticated `gh`, a non-`github.com` remote, or a non-repo directory is classified into a small `reason` enum (`gh-not-installed` / `unauthenticated` / `not-a-github-repo` / `no-remote` / `error`) and degrades to a **cached `available:false` sentinel** — it never throws, never blocks a scan, never spams a toast, and (because the unavailable result is cached too) never re-shells a `gh`-less or non-GitHub repo until the TTL lapses; a non-GitHub remote is decided *before* spawning `gh`. **Security posture:** `gh` is invoked via `execFile("gh", [array, args])` — never a shell string — and the `owner/repo` passed as `-R` is extracted by a pure, unit-tested `parseGitHubRemote` that validates each segment against `^[A-Za-z0-9._-]+$`, so a malformed remote can't smuggle a flag or shell metacharacter. New `GET /api/github-activity` is a dumb cache reader (mirrors `/api/git-status`); the flag-gated enqueue lives at the dashboard-load site (`GET /api/projects`), carrying each project's already-scanned `remoteUrl` so the cache skips a redundant `git remote` call. A new `useGithubActivity` poll hook (mirrors `useGitDirtyStatus`) drives a compact **GitHub strip** on project cards (open-PR / CI-dot / last-push chips, hidden when unavailable) and a fuller strip on the detail Overview tab with an expandable open-PR list; each open PR is best-effort **cross-linked to the Claude session that created it** by joining `gh`'s `repo#number` against the session `prLinks` already harvested by `prExtractor` (presentation-only, no new extraction). Gated behind a new **default-on `githubActivity`** feature flag (default-on costs nothing for `gh`-less users — they already degrade to the silent unavailable state). New `docs/help/github-activity.md` (+ `public/help` mirror) with a cross-reference from `project-details.md`; slug wired into `help-mapping.ts` + `HelpPanel`. Covered by `tests/githubRemote.test.ts` (HTTPS/SSH/SCP shapes, dotted repo names, non-GitHub hosts, and injection attempts → null), `tests/githubActivityCache.test.ts` (happy path, CI mapping, every failure-classification branch, the cached-unavailable no-re-spawn gate, the `-R owner/repo` array-arg regression, and `dispose()` race protection with `gh`/`git` mocked), and `githubActivity` enqueue gating in `tests/api/projectsRoute.test.ts` + meta coverage in `tests/featureFlags.test.ts`.
- **Per-project Operations panel (Portfolio Command Deck — Phase 3).** Each project's detail page gains an **Ops** tab answering "where does this deploy, what does it depend on, what runs on a schedule, and what do I do when it breaks?" — assembled mostly from detection Minder already performs. A new **`OpsSummary` derive layer** (`src/lib/ops/summary.ts`, `deriveOpsSummary`) composes already-scanned fields — `CiCdInfo.hosting`, Vercel + GitHub-Actions schedule crons (merged into one list), `dependabot`, `externalServices`, and `DatabaseInfo` — into one serializable shape with no new scanning; the panel derives it client-side from the project payload (no new API route). Service detection is extended cheaply: `parseDatabaseUrl` now tags a **managed-DB `provider`** from the connection host (Neon `*.neon.tech`, PlanetScale `*.psdb.cloud`, Supabase `*.supabase.co`, Upstash, Railway, Render) and surfaces it in `externalServices`, and dedicated PlanetScale env keys (`PLANETSCALE_DB` / `PSCALE_TOKEN`) are recognized. The curated half is a new **`OPERATIONS.md` runbook** — a living-checklist planning file for the operational truth that can't be auto-detected (backups, monitoring/alerting, on-call/escalation, secrets/rotation, restore) parsed by a tolerant scanner (`src/lib/scanner/operationsMd.ts`): each `##` heading maps to one of the five known section keys via a synonym table, unknown headings pass through as `other`, and completed/obsolete items move to a committed-but-unscanned `OPERATIONS.archive.md` (read on demand via `scanOperationsArchive`). Reading the runbook is gated behind a default-on **`scanOps`** feature flag (neutral when off — auto-detected ops still render; only the curated half drops to "not documented" prompts). The panel surfaces an honest "N of 9 operational facts captured" coverage nudge. New `docs/help/operations.md` (+ `public/help` mirror); tab help wired in `help-mapping.ts`/`HelpPanel`. Covered by `tests/opsSummary.test.ts`, `tests/operationsMd.test.ts`, `tests/envFile.test.ts`, and `scanOps` gating in `tests/featureFlags.test.ts` / `tests/scannerFeatureFlags.test.ts`.
- **View archived TODOs / manual steps.** Completed work moved into the companion `TODO.archive.md` / `MANUAL_STEPS.archive.md` files (which the active scanners deliberately ignore) is now viewable on demand: each project's **TODOs** and **Manual Steps** tabs gain a collapsible **Archived** disclosure at the bottom that lazy-loads the archive read-only the first time it's opened. New on-demand readers `scanTodoArchive` / `scanManualStepsArchive` reuse the existing parsers (so active dashboard counts stay clean); new `GET /api/projects/[slug]/todos/archive` and an `?archived=1` switch on `GET /api/manual-steps/[slug]`; new `ArchivedDisclosure` component. The `TODO.md` parser is refactored to expose a pure `parseTodoMd(content)`. Covered by new tests in `tests/todoMd.test.ts` and `tests/manualStepsMd.test.ts`.
- **Multi-harness ingest — Codex/Gemini sessions now reach the SQLite index (multi-harness TODO item 1, the keystone).** `reconcileAllSessions` (and therefore the ingest watcher's startup reconcile + ~30s sweep) now runs a second, non-Claude pass: it calls `discoverAllSessions(config)`, filters to non-`claude` sources, and ingests each through its adapter's `parseFile` → a new `buildAdapterParsedSession` converter → the existing `writeSession`. Previously the adapter registry's `discover()`/`parseFile()` had **zero callers** — Codex/Gemini parsers existed and were unit-tested but were never connected to ingest, so the By-Source breakdown could only ever hold a single Claude row and the sessions browser only ever held Claude sessions. Now, for adapters listed in `enabledAdapters`, non-Claude sessions are indexed with real per-session/per-turn **cost** (same `applyPricing` formula as Claude), **token** totals, classifier **category**, **work-mode** mix, **one-shot** detection, **tool_uses**, and the real harness session id (Codex `session_meta.payload.id`, Gemini `record.sessionId`) — lighting up the **By Source / By Model / By Project / By Category** usage breakdowns and the **sessions list + detail** (timeline, tools) source filter automatically (the read and aggregation layers were already source-aware). The two long-standing identity bugs are fixed on this path: `source` is taken from the discovered `SessionFile` instead of the literal `"claude"` write, and `sessionId` comes from the adapter-resolved id instead of the filename.

  **Opt-in, zero behavior change by default.** With the default config (`enabledAdapters` unset → `["claude"]`) the non-Claude filter empties and the whole pass is a verified no-op — existing users see byte-identical ingest. A user must enable `codex`/`gemini` in **Settings → Adapters** for their sessions to be indexed; disabling an adapter prunes its sessions on the next scan. A missing `~/.claude/projects` (a Codex/Gemini-only user who never ran Claude) no longer aborts the whole reconcile — it falls through to the adapter pass — while a transient Claude-walk or adapter-discovery failure shields the corresponding existing rows from the prune pass so an enumeration hiccup can never mass-delete indexed data.

  **Known limitation (tracked):** an unknown non-Claude model id with no live pricing match was priced as Claude Sonnet (since hardened to unknown/$0 — see the Fixed entry below, multi-harness item 2). Non-Claude sessions use a "lean" record — full-text prompt-search richness, PR/ticket chips, resume-anomaly/compaction-loop flags, and per-turn context-fill remain Claude-only. New `buildAdapterParsedSession` + `reconcileAdapterSessionFile` in `src/lib/db/ingest.ts`; `ReconcileOptions` gains `config` plus `adapterSessions`/`parseAdapterFile` test seams. Covered by 7 new tests in `tests/dbIngest.test.ts` (pure-conversion of source/sessionId/cost/category/counts, empty→null, end-to-end write of a non-Claude session, unchanged-file skip-gate, prune-on-disable, claude-only no-op default, and the Codex-only-user missing-Claude-tree case). Docs: `docs/help/adapters.md` (+ mirror) gains a "How non-Claude sessions are indexed" section.

- **Harness instruction catalog — Codex `rules`/`AGENTS.md`/`prompts` (plan 007, multi-harness item 5; data layer + API).** A new read-only catalog of harness-native *instruction* artifacts, kept separate from the Claude agents/skills catalogs because they're a different artifact (prose, no model/tools/layout). New `InstructionEntry` type (`kind: "instruction"` plus a `harness` field that is distinct from the filesystem `source`), a `walkCodexInstructions` indexer (Codex `~/.codex/rules/*.{rules,md,txt}`, `prompts/*`, and a top-level `AGENTS.md`; `$CODEX_HOME` honored; fully defensive — a missing home/dir/file contributes nothing), and a config-gated `loadInstructions()` (5-min cache) that surfaces them only when `"codex"` is in `enabledAdapters` (default `["claude"]` → none, matching the opt-in ingest model). New `GET /api/instructions` with `?harness=`/`?source=`/`?q=` filters. Covered by `tests/instructions.test.ts` (walk of rules/prompts/AGENTS.md, frontmatter + slug fallback, dotfile/extension filtering, malformed-frontmatter warnings, and the enabledAdapters gating). **Deferred to follow-ups (tracked in `plans/007`):** the `/instructions` browser UI — this lands the data layer + API first.
- **Harness instruction catalog — Gemini `GEMINI.md` context file (plan 007 follow-up; data layer).** Extends the instruction catalog to Gemini CLI's global context/memory file. New `walkGeminiInstructions` indexer reads the global `GEMINI.md` under the resolved Gemini home (`$GEMINI_HOME` ?? `~/.gemini`, the same rule the Gemini session adapter uses), tagged `harness: "gemini"`, `category: "context"`. The context filename honors a `context.fileName` override in `~/.gemini/settings.json` (newer nested key) with a fallback to the legacy flat `contextFileName`; either may be a single name or a list, in which case the global `GEMINI.md` is preferred. The read is fully defensive — a missing home/file or a missing/malformed `settings.json` contributes nothing and falls back to the default `GEMINI.md`, never throwing. A configured override is validated to a single plain filename (no path separators, `:`, `..`, or absolute paths) before use, so a malicious `settings.json` can't make the walker read a file outside the Gemini home. Gemini's `commands/*.toml` are intentionally excluded for this cut (TOML command defs, not prose). Gated into `loadInstructions()` only when `"gemini"` is in `enabledAdapters`; the cache key now also folds in `$GEMINI_HOME` so a home change is an immediate cache miss. Surfaced via the existing `GET /api/instructions` (`?harness=gemini`). Covered by new cases in `tests/instructions.test.ts` (missing file, frontmatter + slug fallback, string/array/legacy/`malformed` settings overrides, bounded-prefix read, and the enabledAdapters gating including codex+gemini together).

- **`/instructions` browser page — harness-native instruction catalog UI (plan 007 follow-up).** A new cross-project `/instructions` page (sidebar → Library, next to Agents and Skills; also in the command palette) renders the read-only `GET /api/instructions` catalog of harness-native instruction artifacts (Codex `rules`/`AGENTS.md`/`prompts`, Gemini `GEMINI.md`). Each row shows a harness badge (the distinctive control — filter by Codex / Gemini / Claude), category and source badges, a projected-context-cost chip, and a parse-warning indicator; expanding a row reveals the file path, key frontmatter, and body excerpt. Search, source filter (user/plugin/project), and sort (name / recently modified / largest) mirror the Agents browser. Because the catalog is **opt-in** (default `enabledAdapters: ["claude"]` → empty), the empty state explains the feature and links to **Settings → Adapters** to enable Codex/Gemini rather than showing a bare "no results." New `src/components/InstructionsBrowser.tsx` + `src/app/instructions/page.tsx`; nav/help wiring in `AppSidebar`, `AppTopbar`, `commandPalette`, and `help-mapping`; new help doc `docs/help/instructions.md` (+ `public/help` mirror).

- **Board API + scanner integration (Portfolio Command Deck — Phase 1, PR 3).** Each project's git-tracked `BOARD.md` (epics → issues, with stable `^e-`/`^i-` ids, status, priority, `#labels`, and `@wt:`/`~session:` provenance) is now read during the scan and served over a new API. The `scanBoard` feature flag is **wired** (default-on, neutral when off): the scanner orchestrator reads `BOARD.md` per project in its existing parallel batch and attaches `board` to each project. New `GET /api/board` aggregates boards cross-project from the scan cache (like `/api/insights`) with `?project`, `?status`, and `?q` filters — per-issue status/keyword filtering that drops epics emptied by the filter while leaving an unfiltered board untouched. New `GET /api/board/[slug]` returns one project's `BoardInfo` (fresh read, `?archived=1` for the `BOARD.archive.md` done lane); new `POST /api/board/[slug]` mutates via the serializing writer, dispatching `addIssue` / `addEpic` / `setStatus` / `editIssue` / `move` / `reorder` / `promoteTodo`, then invalidates the scan cache. The writer validates `status`/`priority` against their enums at every mutation entry point (rejecting e.g. a stale client's `status:"blocked"` that would otherwise serialize an unreadable `- [undefined] … [blocked]` row and corrupt `BOARD.md`); `BoardWriteError`s map to `404` (NOT_FOUND/BAD_TARGET) or `400` (EMPTY_TITLE/BAD_VALUE). A new `promoteTodoToBoard` writer implements the TODO→board promote path: it reads a `TODO.md` line by number from the canonical main-tree, creates a board issue from its text, and (by default) marks the source todo done — idempotently (a new `setTodoCheckedInFile` sets rather than toggles, so two overlapping promotes can't flip it back open). Board and TODO writes take separate file locks. Slugs resolve to the parent project path via `findProjectPathBySlug`, and the writer canonicalizes again internally, so a worktree path can't slip through to a per-branch copy. Covered by new `promoteTodoToBoard` tests in `tests/boardWriter.test.ts` and `scanBoard` gating in `tests/scannerFeatureFlags.test.ts`.

- **Board UI — cross-project page, per-project tab, and card badge (Portfolio Command Deck — Phase 1, PR 4).** The board feature is now visible. A new **`/board`** page (sidebar → Build, command palette) renders every project's board in one place — issues grouped under their epic with the Inbox as its own lane — with debounced issue search, a status filter, and a project filter; active states (`doing`/`review`/`triage`) use the dashboard's amber attention tokens, done items recede. Each project's detail page gains a **Board** tab (shown once it has a `BOARD.md`) where you can change an issue's status inline (a per-issue dropdown → `POST setStatus`, then refetch) and add an issue straight to the Inbox (`POST addIssue`); issues without a stable `^i-` id show a read-only status chip since mutations target issues by ref. Project cards show a **BoardCompact** badge with the open (non-done) issue count. Shared issue/epic chips (status/priority/label/provenance) live in `BoardChips.tsx`; data hooks in `hooks/useBoard.ts`. New `docs/help/board.md` (+ `public/help` mirror) documents the `BOARD.md` grammar, the TODO→board promote path, the `BOARD.archive.md` done lane, and main-tree canonicalization; route/tab help wired in `help-mapping.ts`, nav in `AppSidebar`/`AppTopbar`/`commandPalette`.

### Fixed
- **Testing-category classification now recognizes `pnpm`/`yarn`/`bun` test runners.** `TESTING_CMD_RE` (`src/lib/usage/classifier.ts`) previously matched only `npm test`/`npm run test` (plus bare runner keywords), so a `pnpm test` / `yarn test` / `bun test` Bash invocation fell through to the "Coding" category — undercounting the Testing category for pnpm/yarn/bun projects (including Project Minder itself). Now matched via a generalized runner prefix.
- **Subagent (Task/sidechain) token cost is now included in usage totals.** Both usage backends (`src/lib/usage/parser.ts` + `aggregator.ts`; `src/lib/db/ingest.ts` + `data/usageFromDb.ts`) previously dropped every subagent turn from token accumulation, so `totalCost`, `totalTokens`, `byModel`, `byProject`, `daily`, and `byCategory` silently under-counted real Claude spend for any subagent-heavy workflow. Subagent turns' input/output/cache tokens and cost now fold into those aggregates and are additionally broken out as new `UsageReport.subagentCost` / `subagentTokens`. They remain excluded from tool/shell/MCP stats, one-shot and self-correction detection, tool transitions, and the activity heatmap/streak/contribution calendar — a subagent turn isn't a user-verified task or independent developer activity. (A1)
- **Usage daily cost chart now buckets by local date instead of UTC.** `aggregator.ts` and `usageFromDb.ts` keyed the daily bars by the UTC date slice while the "today" period filter, streak, and contribution calendar all use local time, so for negative-UTC users a late-evening turn landed on the wrong bar and the "today" total disagreed with the daily bars. Both backends now bucket by the shared `toLocalDateStr` local-date helper so the daily bars, the "today" total, and the contribution calendar agree. (A2)
- **Usage-by-category cost is now attributed to intent categories.** Debugging/Refactoring/Planning/Brainstorming were decided only from `userMessageText`, which the parsers populate on zero-token user turns, so token-bearing assistant turns never landed in those categories and the cost view read ≈0 for them. The triggering user prompt's text is now propagated onto the following assistant turn(s) as `userIntentText`, which the classifier consults, so an assistant turn's cost is attributed to the category its prompt implies. (A3)
- **>200k / 1M-context tiered pricing is now applied.** `costCalculator.applyPricing` did a flat per-token multiply and ignored LiteLLM's `input_cost_per_token_above_200k_tokens` / `output_cost_per_token_above_200k_tokens` surcharge, so large-context turns were under-priced. Token cost now splits at the 200k boundary (base rate up to 200k, surcharge above) when the fields are present, falling back to flat pricing otherwise. (A4)
- **Per-category one-shot rate no longer crosses session boundaries.** The per-category edit→verify→result scan ran over turns grouped only by category, mixing unrelated sessions in scan order; it is now segmented by `sessionId` first, mirroring the headline one-shot logic. (A5)
- **Usage is now de-duplicated by `message.id`.** Both parsers summed every assistant entry with no dedup key, so a re-logged message (retry / resumed-session re-emit) would double-count tokens; a per-session seen-id guard (fallback `requestId`) now skips repeats while keeping genuinely distinct turns. (A6)
- **Cache-hit-rate denominator now includes cache-write tokens** (`cacheRead / (cacheRead + input + cacheWrite)`) so the rate isn't overstated on cache-write-heavy sessions, and the Debugging classifier regex is tightened so bare "fix"/"issue" in ordinary prose ("fix the copy") no longer over-tags Debugging. (A7)
- **Session-quality context-fill % is no longer computed against a 200K window for 1M-default models.** `getModelContextWindow` (`src/lib/usage/sessionQuality.ts`) drove every `opus`/`sonnet`/`haiku` id through a single `200_000` rule, so the current 1M-default models silently resolved to a 5×-too-small window — inflating per-turn context-fill and mis-triggering the compaction-loop detector (a 160K-token turn read as 80% full when it was really ~16%). Separately, `claude-fable-5` matched no rule and logged the one-time `[sessionQuality] unknown model "claude-fable-5"; using default context window 200000` warn. **Fix:** the lookup table now maps the **1M-by-default** models — Fable 5, Mythos 5, Sonnet 5, and the current Opus line (4.6/4.7/4.8) — to 1M ahead of the generic rule, while Sonnet 4.x, Opus 4.5-and-earlier, and Haiku 4.5 keep the conservative 200K default (their 1M SKU is still opted into via the `[1m]` suffix, resolved first). Fable 5 no longer warns. Covered by new cases in `tests/usage/sessionQuality.test.ts` (1M for Fable/Mythos/Sonnet-5 and Opus 4.6–4.8, no-warn for Fable 5, and 200K preserved for Haiku / Sonnet 4.6 / Opus 4.5 with the `[1m]` opt-in still winning).
- **Production builds no longer 500 on every scan-backed route (`/api/projects`, `/api/stats`).** A `pnpm build && pnpm start` (the path `capture:docs:prod` exercises) crashed all scanner-driven routes with `TypeError: The "path" argument must be of type string. Received type number` — so the dashboard, stats, and most prod doc-captures rendered as empty shells while dev mode worked fine. Root cause: `resolveClaudelintBin()` (`src/lib/lint/library.ts`) locates the spawned `claudelint` CLI via `path.dirname(require.resolve("claude-code-lint/package.json"))`; because the package wasn't in `serverExternalPackages`, Turbopack bundled it and rewrote the dynamic `require.resolve(...)` into a **numeric module ID**, so `path.dirname(<number>)` threw. The number was build-stable but build-varying — the signature of a bundler module ID, not a runtime value. **Fix:** added `"claude-code-lint"` to `serverExternalPackages` in `next.config.ts` (the package does a dynamic require and is spawned as a subprocess — exactly what that allowlist is for). **Hardening:** `spawnClaudelint` now resolves the bin path *inside* its Promise with a try/catch, so any future bin-resolution failure honors the wrapper's documented degrade-don't-throw contract (records an `engineError`, returns `[]`) instead of throwing synchronously and taking down the entire scan. Covered by a new degrade test in `tests/lintLibrary.test.ts`.
- **Promoted / delegated tasks now run in their own project directory (PR #227 review).** `runClassicTask` / `runStreamTask` spawned `claude` with no `cwd`, so board-promoted (`promoteBoardIssueToTask`) and TODO-delegated (`delegateTodo`) tasks — both of which store `metadata.projectPath` and default to classic mode — ran in the Minder server's directory and operated on the wrong repo. A new defensive `taskCwd(task)` helper reads `metadata.projectPath` (falling back to `metadata.worktreePath`), validates the directory exists (`fs.existsSync` + `isDirectory`), and is passed as the spawn `cwd`; a stale/missing path or malformed metadata resolves to `undefined` so cron/manual tasks inherit the current cwd unchanged and a bad path never crashes the spawn. Worktree tasks are unaffected — `runWorktreeTask` still wraps `spawnFn` to force the worktree cwd, overriding this. Covered by new cwd tests in `tests/tasksSpawner.test.ts`.
- **GitHub activity polling no longer stops mid-batch, and the detail page now populates the cache (PR #227 review).** Two fixes to the Phase 4 GitHub strip: (1) `githubActivityCache.pending` excluded in-flight work — `processQueue` splices a batch out of the queue *before* its up-to-3 sequential `gh` calls (8s timeouts) finish, so `pending` read 0 mid-batch and the client (which stops on `pending===0 && total>0`, or after ~3 idle polls on a cold cache) could stop polling before results landed. A new `inFlight` counter (incremented when a batch starts, released in a `finally`, zeroed by `dispose()` and generation-guarded against negative drift) is now folded into `pending = queue.length + inFlight`. (2) Only the project **list** route enqueued GitHub activity, so opening `/project/<slug>` directly left the cache empty and the strip never appeared — `GET /api/projects/[slug]` now performs the same flag-gated, git-tracked, remote-carrying enqueue. Covered by new tests in `tests/githubActivityCache.test.ts` and `tests/api/projectsSlugRoute.test.ts`.
- **Session data no longer blanks out on a Windows drive-letter/segment case mismatch (B1).** `scanClaudeSessions` keyed its `history.jsonl` lookup Map with `normalizePath` (slash-swap only, no lowercasing), so a `C:` vs `c:` (or any segment) case difference between what Claude Code recorded as the session's cwd and the scanner's own casing missed the Map lookup entirely — silently blanking `sessionCount`/`lastPrompt`/`lastSessionDate` and demoting the project in activity-sorted views. A new case-insensitive `normalizePathKey` helper (`src/lib/platform.ts`) is now used for both the history-map key and the worktree-session `startsWith` prefix comparison; `normalizePath` itself is unchanged (still used for display). Covered by `tests/claudeSessions.test.ts`.
- **Git panel no longer vanishes for a repo in detached HEAD (B4).** `scanGit` returned `undefined` — discarding commit date/message and remote — whenever `git branch --show-current` returned `""` (detached HEAD, or a zero-commit repo), even though the repo was otherwise perfectly valid. It now falls back to `git rev-parse --short HEAD` as the branch label and keeps populating commit/remote; only a repo with neither a branch nor any commits still resolves to `undefined`. Covered by `tests/git.scanner.test.ts`.
- **A dirty repo whose `git status` invocation fails no longer renders as clean.** `scanGitDirtyStatus` collapsed both "successfully clean" and "git failed (index.lock, timeout, git missing)" to the same `{isDirty:false}`, silently hiding a transient failure as a clean working tree. A new `runGitChecked` distinguishes exec failure from empty stdout, and `scanGitDirtyStatus` now returns an additional optional `unknown: true` flag on failure instead of coercing to clean (existing `isDirty`/`uncommittedCount` shape is unchanged for callers that don't check it). (B5) Covered by `tests/git.scanner.test.ts`.
- **Dev server port detection now recognizes `--port=N` and `-pN` forms.** Both the package.json scanner (`scanPackageJson`) and `processManager.detectDevCommand` matched only whitespace-separated `--port 4100` / `-p 4100`, so `next dev --port=4100` or `vite -p4100` fell through to the framework default — showing the wrong port on the dashboard and missing/spurious port-conflict detection. Both now also match the `=`/no-space forms. (B6) Covered by `tests/packageJson.test.ts` and `tests/processManager.test.ts`.
- **`.env.example` placeholders no longer masquerade as real project metadata.** `scanEnvFiles` read `.env.example` alongside real `.env` files for `DATABASE_URL`/service detection, so a project with only a placeholder `DATABASE_URL` in `.env.example` (and no real `.env`) surfaced a fake database/provider and phantom services in the Operations panel. `.env.example` (and similarly-named template files) is no longer included in the detection source set. (B7) Covered by `tests/envFile.test.ts`.
- **Dashboard status polling backs off when idle instead of looping forever or stopping too early.** `useGitDirtyStatus` previously polled `/api/git-status` every 5s with no stop, so a scope with zero git-tracked projects polled indefinitely. The hooks now: keep the fast 5s cadence while `pending > 0`, stop once enqueued work settles (`total > 0 && pending === 0`), and after a short idle grace (`MAX_IDLE_POLLS`) **back off to a slow 30s heartbeat** rather than stopping. Backing off (not stopping) matters because on a cold load `/api/projects` only enqueues its background checks *after* the project scan completes — a hard stop could fire before that enqueue lands and leave dirty `+N` indicators (or the GitHub strip) unobserved until remount. The same back-off is applied to `useGithubActivity`, which shared the pattern.
- **`manualStepsWatcher` no longer misses new-manual-step notifications when an edit also prunes or archives an older entry.** New-entry detection previously diffed by array position (`newCount > prevCount`, then `slice(prevCount)`), which assumed `MANUAL_STEPS.md` was append-only; under the new living-checklist convention, an edit that removed an entry and added another (count unchanged or lower) produced **no** notification. Detection now diffs by entry **identity** — the `date | slug | title` header signature — via the new pure, unit-tested `manualStepEntryKey` / `diffNewManualStepEntries` helpers, making it robust to pruning, archiving, and reordering (checkbox toggles still correctly produce nothing). Covered by `tests/manualStepsWatcher.test.ts`.
- **Non-Claude model pricing no longer silently bills at Claude Sonnet rates (multi-harness TODO item 2).** `getModelPricing` previously routed *any* model id with no exact/fuzzy/keyword match — including `gpt-*` / `gemini-*` ids while serving the Claude-only offline fallback — to its default Claude Sonnet pricing, so an unpriceable non-Claude session was silently mispriced rather than flagged. The default branch now splits: an unrecognized **Claude-family** id (contains `claude`) still falls back to Sonnet (a reasonable same-family approximation), while an unknown **non-Claude** id is priced as **unknown ($0)** via a new zero-pricing constant — a visible $0 in the By-Source / By-Model / By-Category breakdowns is honest, whereas a fabricated Claude-rate cost is not. No change to the common online path: LiteLLM (refreshed daily) supplies real OpenAI/Google pricing via the exact/fuzzy match, which runs before this branch, so current non-Claude models price correctly. User-defined **pricing rules** still override the result, giving an explicit escape hatch for a specific model. Covered by updated/added tests in `tests/usage/costCalculator.test.ts` (Claude-family unknown → Sonnet; `gpt-*`/`gemini-*`/`o4-*`/unknown → zero; zero-cost turn) plus a deterministic per-turn cost-summation test in `tests/dbIngest.test.ts`. Docs: `docs/help/adapters.md` (+ mirror) pricing note updated.

### Changed
- **Per-route API caches consolidated into one bounded, HMR-safe `TtlCache` (internal perf/robustness — app review C3).** ~18 API route modules (session reports — `agent-network`, `orchestration`, `model-delegation`, `concurrency-timeline`, `handoff`; project reports — `efficiency`, `error-propagation`, `file-coupling`, `git-activity`, `gsd-planning`, `hot-files`, `patterns`; plus `usage`, `usage/compare`, `claude-config`, `plans`, `feedback`, `agent-view/peek`) each hand-rolled the same `globalThis.__xCache ??= new Map()` + manual TTL check + manual sweep-on-write pattern, with no size cap and no HMR-dispose hook — distinct session/project keys accumulated for the server's lifetime. A new `src/lib/routeCache.ts` (`TtlCache<T>` + `getOrCreateRouteCache`/`disposeAllRouteCaches`, registry pinned to `globalThis` so state survives dev HMR) replaces all of them: same TTL per route (unchanged), LRU eviction past `maxEntries` (80%-trim sweep, mirroring `FileCache.evictIfNeeded`), and a `dispose()`/registry hook for future HMR/reset wiring. Every migrated route's TTL, cache key shape, and ETag/mtime-invalidation logic is unchanged — this is a mechanical consolidation, not a behavior change. `sessions/activity` was left on its hand-rolled cache (it shares a `globalThis` slot with `/api/sessions` and the RSC session prefetch; migrating one side without the other would break that sharing). The two SSE client-registry routes (`events`, `agent-view/stream`) are untouched — they aren't value caches. Also added the missing `dispose()`/generation guard to `skillUpdateCache` (mirroring `efficiencyGradeCache`/`gitStatusCache`) so an in-flight `processQueue` can't resurrect entries after a dispose. Covered by new `tests/routeCache.test.ts` (TTL expiry, maxEntries eviction, HMR-reuse, dispose) and `tests/skillUpdateCacheDispose.test.ts` (dispose race protection).
- **Catalog project walk now batches instead of firing an unbounded `Promise.all` (internal perf — app review C5).** `loadCatalog` (`src/lib/indexer/catalog.ts`) fanned out one concurrent directory walk per project with no limit — at ~61 projects that's 61 concurrent walks competing for file descriptors. It now walks in batches sized by the same `config.scanBatchSize` (default 10) the scanner already uses for its own project fan-out, flattening results in project order (output content and effective ordering unchanged).
- **Efficiency-grade batch computation no longer re-scans the full session map per project (internal perf — app review C5).** `efficiencyGradeCache.processQueue` called `gatherProjectTurns(sessionMap, slug, path)` — an O(sessions) full-map filter — once per queued project, an O(projects × sessions) cost per drain cycle. A new `buildProjectTurnsIndex`/`lookupProjectTurns` pair (`src/lib/usage/projectMatch.ts`) indexes the session map once per drain (by both `projectSlug` and `projectDirName`, the same two match keys `gatherProjectTurns` checks) and looks up each project in O(1); computed grades are unchanged. `gatherProjectTurns` itself is untouched for its single-lookup callers (the per-request report routes). Covered by new index-vs-scan parity tests in `tests/projectMatch.test.ts`.
- **CI now runs a Node 20/22 matrix on Ubuntu, asserts the `better-sqlite3` native driver actually loaded, and adds an advisory Windows job.** `.github/workflows/ci.yml`'s `verify` job gains `strategy.matrix.node-version: ['20.19.0', '22.12.0']` (`fail-fast: false`) so both ends of the `engines` range are exercised, not just 20. A new "Assert better-sqlite3 native driver loaded" step runs right after install and before tests, so a native-build failure now fails CI loudly instead of silently skipping the ~34 DB-backed test suites while the job still reports green. A separate `verify-windows` job (same install→lint→typecheck→test→build steps) runs on `windows-latest` for advisory coverage of the Windows-targeted app; it's marked `continue-on-error: true` so a Windows-only build-tooling gap can't block the required `verify` check.
- **The local pre-commit hook now runs lint too.** `scripts/setup-hooks.mjs`'s installed hook is now `pnpm lint && pnpm typecheck && pnpm test --pool=forks` (lint first, since it's fastest to fail) instead of typecheck+test only, matching what CI enforces. Documented in `README.md` and `CONTRIBUTING.md`.
- **The three bespoke pollers now ride the SSE stream instead of their own timers (Performance P3 — PR #243).** Building on the SSE stream (PR #242), the pollers that aren't TanStack-Query-backed — **`useGitDirtyStatus`**, **`useGithubActivity`**, and the app-wide **`PulseProvider`** — now refetch on pushed events rather than on a fixed interval (still behind the default-off `liveEvents` flag). Because `invalidateQueries` can't reach these `useState`+`fetch` hooks, PR #242's `LiveEventsBridge` was generalized into a **`LiveEventsProvider`** (one EventSource for the whole app) that both invalidates query keys AND fans each event out to non-Query subscribers via a new **`useLiveEvent(type, handler)`** hook. Two new events carry the git/github signals — **`git-status.updated`** and **`github-activity.updated`**, emitted by `gitStatusCache`/`githubActivityCache` each time a background batch lands — so `useGitDirtyStatus`/`useGithubActivity` drop their 5s interval entirely and refetch exactly when fresh results exist (the interval + idle-backoff path is preserved unchanged as the flag-off fallback). `PulseProvider` refetches on `scan.invalidated` (manual steps) + `sessions.changed` (live-session activity) and, since a few of its fields have no event (dispatcher/CLI availability), keeps a **safety-net timer slowed from 5s → 20s** when the flag is on (its `poll()` is single-flighted, so event- and timer-driven refetches collapse safely). With the flag off, all three poll exactly as before. New `useLiveEvent` + `git-status.updated`/`github-activity.updated` covered in `tests/events.test.ts`. This completes the Performance P3 polling-consolidation work.
- **Pages can refresh in real time over one SSE stream instead of polling (Performance P3 — PR #242).** Behind a new **default-off `liveEvents`** feature flag (Settings → Active features), the client opens a single **`/api/events`** Server-Sent Events stream and, on each pushed signal, calls TanStack Query's `invalidateQueries` for the mapped resources — so data-heavy pages update the moment something changes rather than on a timer. A new in-process **event bus** (`src/lib/events/bus.ts`, a `globalThis` `EventEmitter` mirroring `agentView/eventBus`) carries two coarse signals — **`sessions.changed`** (emitted from the ingest write path in `db/ingest.ts`) and **`scan.invalidated`** (emitted from `invalidateCache()`, the single choke point every scan-mutating path already calls, so it covers manual-steps, insights, and stats in one event). The SSE route (`src/app/api/events/route.ts`) follows the existing `agent-view/stream` template — `ReadableStream`, 15s keepalive comments, `X-Accel-Buffering: no`, and cleanup driven by `request.signal` — plus **per-type coalescing (250ms)** so a burst (e.g. a startup ingest sweep) collapses into one client-visible event. The client bridge (`src/components/LiveEventsBridge.tsx`, mounted once inside `QueryProvider`) is inert unless the flag is on, and the **event→query-key map** (`src/lib/events/invalidation.ts`) is a pure, unit-tested function returning prefix keys (so `["sessions"]` invalidates the list and every open detail in one call). When the flag is on, **`useAllSessions` drops its 15s `refetchInterval`** (the `sessions.changed` event drives it instead); when off, everything polls/refetches exactly as before — the merge is a no-op until you opt in. `invalidateQueries` only refetches *mounted* queries, so events for pages you aren't viewing cost nothing. This is the first of two SSE steps; the bespoke `/api/pulse`, git-status, and github-activity pollers followed in PR #243. New `src/lib/events/{types,bus,invalidation}.ts`; covered by `tests/events.test.ts` (bus emit/subscribe/unsubscribe, the event→prefix map, and the `liveEvents` default-off guard).
- **The two live mutations can now run as Server Actions instead of API routes (Performance P3 — PR #241).** Behind a new **default-off `serverActions`** feature flag (Settings → Active features), the two writes a user actually triggers — **toggling a manual step** and **changing a project's status** — go through Next.js **Server Actions** (`toggleManualStepAction` / `setProjectStatusAction` in `src/lib/server/actions.ts`) rather than `POST /api/manual-steps/[slug]` / `PUT /api/config`. Each action is a thin `'use server'` wrapper over a plain core mutation in `src/lib/server/mutations/{manualSteps,projectStatus}.ts`; the **existing API routes were refactored to delegate to those same core functions**, so the route path and the action path are behaviourally identical by construction and can't drift. With the flag off (the default) every mutation uses the API route exactly as before — the merge is a no-op until you opt in. Net effect when on: one fewer client `fetch` hop per write (the call runs in the same server module as the writer), and — the visible win — the project-detail status change **no longer forces a full `window.location.reload()`**; it writes and re-fetches just that project (a new `refresh` on `useProject`). The client callers (`useToggleStep`, `useProjects.updateStatus`, and the project-detail `handleStatusChange`) branch on the flag via `useConfig()` + `getFlag(..., false)`, keeping the existing optimistic UI (the manual-step optimistic Map, the dashboard's optimistic `setData`) intact on both paths. Covered by `tests/serverMutations.test.ts` (core-mutation behaviour: project-not-found → `ProjectNotFoundError`, correct `MANUAL_STEPS.md` path + cache invalidation, non-numeric line guard, `statuses[slug]` write + both cache invalidations) and the `serverActions` default-off meta guard; `serverActions` meta coverage also runs in `tests/featureFlags.test.ts`.
- **Read-heavy pages can now render with their data server-side (Performance P3 — PR #240, async RSC + HydrationBoundary).** Behind a new **default-off `rscHydration`** feature flag (Settings → Active features), the ten data pages — `sessions`, `usage`, `stats`, `agents`, `skills`, `insights`, `commands`, `manual-steps`, `templates`, `config` — become async React Server Components that **prefetch their data on the server**, dehydrate it, and stream it into the client TanStack Query cache via `<HydrationBoundary>`. The client island's existing `useQuery` then reads from the already-warm cache, so the page **paints with data instead of a loading spinner and fires no first-mount round-trip**; each route also gets a `loading.tsx` skeleton that streams instantly while the server prefetch runs. With the flag off, every page renders exactly as before (the boundary becomes a transparent pass-through and the client fetches on mount) — so the merge is a no-op until you opt in. **Parity is enforced by construction:** server prefetch and client fetch share the same `queryKeys` factory (the server fills the exact cache entry the client reads); each route's response-body assembly is extracted into a shared `src/lib/server/queries/<resource>.ts` loader that *both* the API route and the prefetch call (no duplicated filter logic to drift); and every server-prefetched value is JSON-cloned so it is byte-identical to what `await res.json()` yields client-side (neutralizing the Flight-serializes-`Date`-as-`Date` hydration footgun). The flag gate, the per-request server `QueryClient`, and the clone live in one `maybeDehydrate()` helper (`src/lib/server/prefetch.ts`) so each page is a two-liner. As part of this, the **four pages that PR 1 left on bespoke fetch hooks were migrated onto TanStack Query** (new `commandsQuery`/`templatesQuery`/`manualStepsQuery`/`configQuery` factories + `useQuery`-backed hooks, with identical public shapes and the config catalog's per-tab `enabled`-gated query preserved), so all ten now share one data-fetching path. Page titles moved from the client `useDocumentTitle` hook to RSC `metadata` (rendered server-side, no flash). New deps: none. Covered by `tests/rscHydration.test.ts` (prefetch↔client queryKey parity for every resource, `jsonClone` JSON-equivalence, `maybeDehydrate` flag gating, and the four new factories' key/URL shapes) plus the existing route/parser suites the shared loaders are exercised by.
- **Hover now warms list/detail data so navigations land on cached data (Performance P3 — PR #239, hover prefetch).** Hovering (or keyboard-focusing) a sidebar nav item or a session row now prefetches that destination's data into the TanStack Query cache, so the page it links to usually mounts from cache instead of waiting on a fresh round-trip. Next.js's `<Link>` already prefetches the route bundle + RSC payload on hover, but our pages are `"use client"` and fetch their data in `useQuery` *after* mount — so the data stayed cold; this closes that gap. A new `useHoverPrefetch` hook (`src/hooks/useHoverPrefetch.ts`) calls `queryClient.prefetchQuery` and is **safe to fire on every hover**: it passes the client's default `staleTime` (30s) explicitly — `prefetchQuery` does *not* inherit it otherwise — so a list hovered within the last 30s is a no-op rather than a redundant request, and prefetch errors are swallowed (the destination page's real `useQuery` owns error reporting/retries). To guarantee the warm request is byte-for-byte the request the page's hook makes, each migrated query's `{ queryKey, queryFn }` is extracted into a shared **`src/lib/queryOptions.ts`** factory (idiomatic v5 `queryOptions()`), and the six PR 1 hooks (`useAllSessions`/`useSessionDetail`, `useStats`, `useUsage`, `useAgents`, `useSkills`, `useAllInsights`/`useProjectInsights`) now consume those factories — a pure refactor with **identical public return shapes** (the `AgentRow`/`SkillRow` types moved to `queryOptions.ts` and are re-exported from the hooks, so no consumer import changed). Wired into the sidebar nav (`/sessions`, `/stats`, `/usage` warming the dashboard's default 30d period, `/agents`, `/skills`, `/insights`) and `SessionsBrowser` rows (warming `/api/sessions/[id]`). The two detail factories (`sessionDetailQuery`/`insightDetailQuery`) treat a **404 as a cacheable `null`** ("genuinely not found") but **throw on any other non-OK**, so a transient failure during a warm is recorded as a query error and refetched on click rather than cached as fresh `null` (which would otherwise pin "not found" for the 30s stale window even after the API recovered). Net effect: snappier navigation with no UI, API-shape, or behavior change. Covered by `tests/queryOptions.test.ts` (every factory's key shape, the exact request its `queryFn` fires, and the 404-`null`-vs-throw contract for the detail factories).
- **Client data fetching now runs on TanStack Query (Performance P3 — PR 1, the foundation).** A new `QueryProvider` (`src/components/QueryProvider.tsx`) is mounted in the root layout between `ConfigProvider` and `PulseProvider`, configured for a local dashboard: `staleTime: 30s` (cross-page navigation and remounts serve from cache instead of refetching), `gcTime: 5min` (inactive query data is garbage-collected so long-lived sessions stay memory-stable), `refetchOnWindowFocus: false`, and `retry: 1`. It uses the documented App-Router client pattern — a fresh `QueryClient` per server render, a browser-singleton on the client — so PR 3's RSC `HydrationBoundary` slots in without a provider refactor. The React Query Devtools are wired dev-only (code-split via `next/dynamic`, gated on `NODE_ENV`, never shipped to production). Six read-only fetch hooks were rewritten to `useQuery` behind **identical public return shapes** (`{ data, loading, refresh }`), so no consuming component changed: `useAllSessions`/`useSessionDetail`, `useStats`, `useUsage`, `useAgents`, `useSkills`, and `useAllInsights`/`useProjectInsights`. `useAllSessions` preserves its 15s live-refresh via `refetchInterval` (auto-paused while the tab is hidden); `refresh` maps to the stable `refetch` so consumer effect-deps don't churn. Cache keys are centralized in a new pure, unit-tested `src/lib/queryKeys.ts` factory (namespaced list/detail, optional params normalized to `null`) shared by the upcoming hover-prefetch (PR 2) and SSE invalidation (PR 5) phases. Net effect: per-resource request de-duplication and stale-while-revalidate caching with no UI or API-shape change. New deps: `@tanstack/react-query`, `@tanstack/react-query-devtools` (dev). Covered by `tests/queryKeys.test.ts`.
- **Planning writes are now canonical to the main working tree (worktree-fragmentation fix, foundation for the Portfolio Command Deck).** Planning files (`TODO.md` / `MANUAL_STEPS.md` / `INSIGHTS.md`) are project-scoped, not branch-scoped. A new `resolveCanonicalProjectPath(cwd, devRoots)` helper (`src/lib/canonicalProjectPath.ts`) maps a git-worktree checkout (`…--claude-worktrees-…`) back to its parent project — worktree and parent are siblings, with the configured dev roots as a safety boundary (a path that resolves outside every dev root is refused and treated as canonical, never redirected).
