The TODO and manual-steps writers — `appendTodosToFile` / `toggleTodoInFile` (`todoWriter.ts`) and `toggleStepInFile` (`manualStepsWriter.ts`) — route through it, so a write originating from a worktree lands in the canonical file instead of fragmenting into a per-branch copy. `appendInsights` (`scanner/insightsMd.ts`) is deliberately **not** canonicalized: its internal caller `syncInsightsFromSessions` extracts a worktree's own session insights and must write them to that worktree's `INSIGHTS.md` to feed the worktree overlay; worktree→parent reconciliation for insights stays the job of the worktree-sync route. This is a no-op for current callers (the API routes already resolve slugs to the parent `project.path`); its purpose is to make the invariant *"a Minder writer never touches a worktree planning copy"* true by construction, ahead of the Phase 2 MCP write-bridge which will receive worktree `cwd`s. The recently-shipped worktree-sync route + overlay are unchanged (prevention and reconciliation coexist). Agent guidance (CLAUDE.md + the propagated Setup Guide in `src/lib/setup-content.ts`) gains a rule to log planning to the canonical main-tree file when working in a worktree. Covered by `tests/canonicalProjectPath.test.ts`.
- **`TODO.md` / `MANUAL_STEPS.md` are now living checklists, not append-only logs.** The CLAUDE.md guidance blocks — and the Setup Guide content in `src/lib/setup-content.ts` that propagates them to your other projects, plus `docs/help/{manual-steps,setup}.md` — now instruct agents to keep these files lean: check off or prune done work, and move completed/obsolete entries into companion `TODO.archive.md` / `MANUAL_STEPS.archive.md` files (committed for the historical record, but ignored by the scanners so active counts stay clean) rather than letting finished work pile up or silently deleting it. `INSIGHTS.md` is deliberately unchanged — it remains an append-only log. No format change: the checkbox + dated-header format and the Setup Guide's generated validator hooks (format-only, exact-filename-scoped) are untouched, and `*.archive.md` is exempt by name.
- **Codex & Gemini adapters now implement `parseFileWithMeta` (interface parity — multi-harness TODO item 4).** The optional `SessionAdapter.parseFileWithMeta(file) → { turns, meta: SessionTurnsMeta }` was previously implemented only by the Claude adapter. Codex and Gemini now implement it too: each `parseFile` is refactored to delegate to a shared `parse<Harness>FileWithMeta` helper (returning `.turns`), so existing turn-parsing behavior is unchanged. Meta is derived per harness — `cliVersion` from Codex `session_meta.cli_version` (else the most-frequent per-entry `version`) and Gemini's top-level `version` (else null); `hasThinking` from a Codex assistant `thinking` block or a Gemini message's non-empty `thoughts`; `compactBoundaries` is always `[]` (a Claude-only concept). No user-visible behavior change — `parseFileWithMeta` has no caller yet (it exists for a future session-detail/meta consumer); this just closes the interface-parity gap. Covered by new tests in `tests/codexAdapter.test.ts` and `tests/geminiAdapter.test.ts` (WithMeta turns match `parseFile`, meta shape, source stamping, and positive thinking/version cases).

### Security
- **New Origin/Host middleware closes the localhost cross-site API surface (app-review finding S1, plus S2–S5).** Project Minder is intentionally no-auth (local-only tool), but until now nothing checked *who* could reach `http://localhost:4100/api/*` — any site open in your browser could drive dev-server start/stop, board mutations, config changes (including widening `devRoots`), and read the entire local index via `/api/sql`, and a DNS-rebinding attacker could reach the same surface from a hostile page. A new **`src/middleware.ts`** (scoped to `/api/:path*` via `config.matcher`) adds two layered checks: (1) a **Host allowlist** (`localhost`/`127.0.0.1`/`[::1]`, all at `:4100`) applied to every method, including GET, so read endpoints like `/api/sql` can't be reached via DNS rebinding; (2) an **Origin allowlist** applied to **every** method (including GET/HEAD) — if `Origin` is present it must match the same allowlist (defeats CSRF), but an absent `Origin` is allowed through (non-browser clients like curl or the MCP server's own tools never send one). Because an origin-less cross-site GET (an `<img>` subresource sends a valid `Host` but no `Origin`) can't be caught by the Origin check, side-effecting GETs were removed at the source too — the task dispatcher now starts at server boot (`instrumentation-node.ts`) instead of on a GET to `/api/tasks` or `/api/swarms`. `/api/mcp` is exempted entirely since it already enforces its own DNS-rebinding protection via the MCP SDK transport. The pure decision logic is exported as `evaluateRequest()` for direct unit testing (`tests/middleware.test.ts`). This single middleware closes S1, S3 (`/api/sql` Host check), and S5 (`devRoots` widening is now Origin-protected; one-line comment added at the patch site in `src/app/api/config/route.ts`).
- **`port` is now runtime-validated before it can reach a process spawn (finding S2).** `POST /api/dev-server/[slug]` typed the request body's `port` as `number` but never validated it at runtime; an attacker-supplied string/float/out-of-range value could reach `processManager.start`/`restart` → `String(portOverride)` → the `spawn` args in `src/lib/platform.ts`. The route now rejects (`400 {error:"port must be an integer 1-65535"}`) anything but a genuine integer in 1–65535 for both `start` and `restart`, before `processManager` is called. A defense-in-depth `sanitizePort()` guard was also added inside `processManager.start`/`restart` so a non-integer portOverride from any other caller is treated as "no override" rather than reaching the spawn args. Covered by new cases in `tests/api/devServerRoute.test.ts` (`0`, `70000`, `"4100&calc"`, `3.5`, `NaN` all rejected; a valid `4100` passes through).
- **`processManager.start()` no longer has a check-then-act race that can orphan a dev-server child process (finding S4).** `start()` checked `isRunning(slug)` at entry but only registered the process in `this.processes` after `detectDevCommand` resolved and a 2000ms readiness timer elapsed, so two overlapping `start()` calls for the same slug could both pass the entry check and both spawn — the first child was silently overwritten in the map, never tracked, and never killed by `stop()`. `start()` now inserts a synchronous `"starting"` placeholder into `this.processes` immediately after the `isRunning()` check (before the first `await`), so a concurrent call observes it and returns early instead of racing; the placeholder is removed if `detectDevCommand` throws or the target port turns out to be in use. Covered by a new concurrency test in `tests/processManager.test.ts` asserting two overlapping `start()` calls for one slug produce exactly one spawn.

## [1.1.0] - 2026-05-31

### Added
- **Read-only Codex CLI config surface (TODO item 1).** A new **Harnesses** page (sidebar → Review, route `/adapters`) shows a read-only view of an enabled harness's own config home. The `SessionAdapter` interface gains an optional `readConfig?(): Promise<HarnessConfig>`; the Codex adapter implements it by reading `~/.codex/config.toml` (parsed with the new `smol-toml` dependency), `rules/` instruction files (content capped), and presence flags for notable subdirs (`memories`/`plugins`/`automations`/`prompts`) — resolving the home via `$CODEX_HOME` ?? `~/.codex`, the same rule session discovery uses. Claude/Gemini leave `readConfig` undefined (no behavior change). **Secret redaction is the security core**: the parsed config object is walked and redacted *before* it leaves the server — secret tables (`http_headers`/`headers`/`env`/`auth`/`credentials`) are blanked wholesale, scalars under secret-looking keys (authorization/token/api_key/password/…) are blanked, and a value-shape backstop catches tokens hiding under innocent keys (bearer/`sk-`/`napi_`/`gh*_`/JWT/long-hex). Keys are kept so you can see *that* something is configured, just not its value; `auth.json` is never read; large files (`logs_2.sqlite`, `archived_sessions/`) are never touched. New `GET /api/adapters/[id]/config` (returns **404, never 500**, for unknown / no-readConfig / not-enabled harnesses; the adapter read path is degrade-silent so a missing or unparseable config yields `present:false` / `parseError`, never a throw); the existing `GET /api/adapters` now also reports `enabled` + `hasConfig` per harness (array shape preserved). View-only by design — no edit/copy/share affordance. Explicitly deferred to a later cross-harness wave: config editing, per-harness timestamped backups, and security scanning for non-Claude harnesses. New `src/lib/adapters/redact.ts`, `HarnessConfig` types, `HarnessConfigView` component; covered by `tests/codexConfig.test.ts` (fs-mocked: missing home, parse + redaction of the real secret shapes, `CODEX_HOME` precedence, parse-error degradation, rules cap) and `tests/redactConfig.test.ts` (table/key/value-shape redaction, nested structure preservation, no-mutation).
- **Efficiency-grade trends (new/improving/declining/stable) via daily snapshots (TODO item 4b).** Each project's efficiency grade (A–F) is now snapshotted once per calendar day to a new `project_grade_snapshots` table (migration **v16**; mirrored in `schema.sql`), and the dashboard classifies a **trend** by comparing today's freshly-computed grade against the most-recent *prior-day* snapshot. The project-detail Efficiency tab shows a worded badge (`↑ improving` / `↓ declining` / `= stable` / `• new`); the dashboard project cards show a compact green ↑ / red ↓ arrow next to the grade letter (the actionable letter-movement signals only). The trend is classified on grade **letter** movement so the card and detail views never disagree; finding counts (high/med/low) are stored per snapshot as the row's substance but don't drive the label. Writes are best-effort from the existing efficiency-grade cache (bulk) and the per-project efficiency route (single), through one shared idempotent upsert keyed on `(project_slug, snapshot_date)` — a same-day re-run overwrites that day's row, never duplicates it. New `GradeTrend` data layer (`src/lib/data/gradeSnapshots.ts`); `/api/efficiency-grades` gains a `trends` map and `/api/projects/[slug]/efficiency` gains a `trend` field. Snapshots are **forward-only** (no `DERIVED_VERSION` bump): history accrues from first run rather than being backfilled, so trends populate over days. Entirely degrade-silent — `MINDER_USE_DB=0` or any DB error yields no trend indicator and never affects grade serving. Deviations from the plan: dropped the planned `score` column (derivable from the stored counts) and use project-grade-granularity labels (the plan's per-finding "resolved" needs per-finding rows, which this snapshot deliberately doesn't store). Covered by `tests/gradeSnapshot.test.ts` (classification, local snapshot-date formatting, cross-day improving/declining/stable, most-recent-prior selection, upsert idempotency, bulk classification, and DB-off degradation) plus a `project_grade_snapshots` assertion in the fresh-DB migration test.
- **Period-over-period comparison on the Usage dashboard (TODO item 4a).** A new **Compare** toggle in the `/usage` toolbar overlays a delta strip above the summary cards, diffing the current period against the immediately preceding window of equal length (last 7d vs the 7d before, etc.). It deltas exactly the five metrics already on screen — Total Cost, Tokens, Sessions, Cache Hit, One-Shot Rate — so no metric is invented for the comparison: volume metrics (cost/tokens/sessions) show relative % in a neutral tone (a prior-empty window reads **new**); quality metrics (cache hit, one-shot) show the percentage-*point* change colored green/red by direction. Windows are computed from a single injected instant using **elapsed** duration rather than nominal period length, which makes **Today** honest — at 9am the partial morning is compared against the equal-length block ending at midnight, not against a full previous day. The comparison is pure SQL over already-indexed columns (no migration): a focused two-query summary per window (`compareUsageFromSql` → `queryPeriodSummary`), deliberately *not* the full `loadUsageReportFromSql`, whose streak/calendar/heatmap aggregates ignore the period filter and would be identical across both windows. New `GET /api/usage/compare?period=&project=&source=` (mtime-salted ETag, mirrors `/api/usage`) and a `useUsageCompare` hook. SQL-only by nature: Compare is hidden for **All Time** (no prior window) and resolves to a `comparable: false` result with an explanatory reason when `MINDER_USE_DB=0` or during the v3-reconcile catch-up window (rather than reporting misleading ~0 cost deltas). Note: this implements item 4a's *intent* with a `compare(period)` current-vs-prior shape, deviating from the plan's sketched `?a=&b=` two-arbitrary-period signature — two rolling windows can't express a non-overlapping period-over-period comparison. Covered by `tests/usageCompare.test.ts` (window split, delta math, the `new`/null-pct case, equal-length `today` windows, `all` not-comparable, project-filter threading, and the façade's not-comparable branches).
- **ClaudeLint follow-ups: strict gate + interactive formatter on the Config Lint tab (TODO item 5).** Two additions to the read-only lint surface, both gated behind the existing `configLint` feature flag. (1) **Strict gate** — `LintReport` gains a materialized `hasBlocking` boolean (computed once in `buildReport`: `true` when any P0/P1 finding exists) so the "does this config clear the bar" contract lives in exactly one place and rides along in every API/MCP response rather than being re-derived per consumer. The Config Lint panel header renders a green **STRICT: PASS** / red **STRICT: FAIL** badge from it; P2-only configs pass. (2) **Formatter** — a `Check formatting` → `Apply` control wrapping the library-owned `claudelint format` (markdownlint + prettier; shellcheck when installed). Check (`--fix-dry-run`) is non-mutating and lists which Claude files would be rewritten; Apply **snapshots each target to Config History via `recordPreWrite` before** the mutating `--fix`, so every format is reversible, and reports per-file what actually changed (files the formatter left untouched have their redundant backup rolled back). Apply only ever runs on the explicit button click — never during a scan. New `src/lib/lint/format.ts` (`checkFormatting`, `applyFormatting`) + `POST /api/config-lint/[slug]/format` (`{ mode: "check" | "apply" }`, slug→path resolved server-side so only scanned project dirs can be mutated). The `claudelint` bin resolution is now shared via `resolveClaudelintBin()` exported from `lint/library.ts`.

  **Why no per-finding autofix.** The original item-5 plan proposed an `autofix?()` capability keyed to the CLAUDE.md audit findings. Reading the seven audit codes (`long-index`, `file-size`, `inline-bloat`, `missing-topic-files`, `rules-volume`, `reference-tiering`, `no-claude-md`) showed every one requires human judgment about *what content to extract and where* — none has a safe mechanical rewrite. Building the framework would have shipped a capability with zero safe callers. Instead the *formatter* is the mechanical writer, the "Fix" affordance just runs it, and structural findings stay advisory (carrying their existing guidance text). Delegating to prettier (rather than a hand-rolled `JSON.parse → stringify`) also avoids silently destroying JSONC comments/trailing commas in `settings.json`. 11 new tests: `tests/lintFormat.test.ts` (8 — dry-run file-list parsing, clean/empty, spawn-error degrade, non-mutating-mode assertion, snapshot-before-fix ordering, unchanged-file backup rollback, no-fix-when-clean, error propagation) + 3 strict-gate cases in `tests/lintEngine.test.ts`.
- **Session ↔ ticket linking — Linear / Jira / GitHub-issue chips on the project Sessions tab (TODO item 3).** Each session row now shows a ticket chip per distinct issue-tracker URL it references — `ENG-123` (Linear), `PROJ-45` (Jira), or `owner/repo#42` (GitHub issue) — alongside the existing PR chips. Clicking a chip filters the in-page list to sessions referencing that ticket, with the same banner + clear-filter affordance as PR chips; selecting a ticket clears any active PR filter (and vice versa) so the two filters never AND down to an empty list. New `GET /api/sessions?ticket=<url>` exact-URL filter mirrors `?pr=` (and is folded into the ETag salt so 304s stay correct across filter switches).

  **Design — referenced, not created.** Unlike PRs (harvested from the *output* of a `gh pr create` command, matched call→result by `tool_use_id`), a ticket reference is meaningful wherever it appears. New pure module `src/lib/usage/ticketExtractor.ts` (`extractTicketsFromText`, `extractTicketsFromEntries`, `compareTicketLinks`; the `TicketLink`/`TicketProvider` types live in `src/lib/types.ts`) therefore scans **all** session text — user prompts, assistant text, and tool_result output (so a `gh issue create` result is picked up for free) — for full tracker URLs and dedupes by canonical URL. This drops the `tool_use_id` pairing AND the tail-straddle recovery the PR path needs: there is no cross-cursor call/result case, so tickets in already-persisted bytes are simply carried forward by a `preservedTickets` merge on every rewrite (the ticket analogue of `mergePrLinks`). Provider, key, and canonical link all derive from the URL itself (Linear `linear.app/<ws>/issue/<KEY>`, Jira `<host>/browse/<KEY>` where host must contain a dot, GitHub `github.com/<owner>/<repo>/issues/<N>` — `/issues/` only, so PR URLs never match; trailing slug/anchor/query stripped; `issues/0` and `issues/42x` rejected).

  **Scope — full URLs only (bare keys deferred).** This narrows the original TODO-item-3 plan, which also proposed matching bare keys (`[A-Z]{2,10}-\d+`, `#N`) from branch names and commit messages. Those are the false-positive-prone case (`UTF-8`, `#123` in code) and the only part that needs per-workspace `ticketProviders` config to build a URL, so they are split into a follow-up. Full URLs are self-validating, so the shipped extractor is effectively false-positive-free.

  New DB migration **v15** adds `session_tickets (session_id, url, provider, ticket_key)` — composite PK `(session_id, url)`, `WITHOUT ROWID`, `FK ON DELETE CASCADE` to `sessions`, index `session_tickets_by_url` powering the `?ticket=` lookup — mirrored in `schema.sql` and the `sqlSchemaSnapshot.ts` snapshot. `DERIVED_VERSION` → **9** so the existing corpus is re-parsed once and backfilled (forward-only otherwise). Both ingest paths (`writeSession` full-rewrite with preserve-then-merge, and the tail-append fast path) `INSERT OR IGNORE`; both read paths are wired — `loadSessionsListFromDb` adds one batched `SELECT ... FROM session_tickets` to populate `SessionSummary.tickets` (the chips render from here), and `loadSessionDetailFromDb` surfaces `SessionDetail.tickets` for API/MCP parity. The file-parse backend (`scanSessionFile`) extracts tickets too, so chip order/content is identical across backends (sorted `provider, ticket_key, url`). 20 tests in `tests/ticketExtractor.test.ts` cover each provider's URL shape, slug/anchor/query stripping, PR-URL rejection, bare-key/`#N` non-matching (deferred scope), single-label-host rejection, dedup + sort, and entry-walking across string prompts, array text blocks, assistant text, and tool_result content.
- **Two new Claude Code data sources: `stats-cache.json` cross-check + rich `session-meta` surface (TODO: cc-lens-inspired).** New read-only scanner module `src/lib/scanner/claudeStats.ts` reads two files Claude Code maintains under `~/.claude` that the dashboard didn't previously surface, both parsed **defensively** (a missing *or malformed* file degrades to `null` rather than throwing — the deliberate difference from `claudeFacets.ts`, since these decorate pages that must never break). (1) **`stats-cache.json`** — Claude's own aggregate counter. `getStatsCache()` + the pure `crossCheckStats(stats, observed)` helper compare our independently-computed totals against Claude's; `/api/stats` now returns a `crossCheck` block (`StatsCrossCheck` on `StatsData`) and the `/stats` Claude-Usage section renders a **Cross-check card** showing our number vs Claude's with a colour-coded drift % (green <5%, amber <20%, red beyond). Both rows compare like-for-like counts (sessions vs sessions; our summed per-session message count vs Claude's message tally). Hidden when the file is absent. The stats-cache read runs concurrently with the sessions fetch. (2) **`usage-data/session-meta/<id>.json`** — a rich per-session metadata record. `getSessionMeta(sessionId)` maps Claude's snake_case fields to a camelCase `SessionMeta` (git commits/pushes, lines added/removed, files modified, interruptions, tool-error categories, capability-usage flags, durations, first prompt). Attached to `SessionDetail.sessionMeta` in the `getSessionDetail` data façade (above both the DB and file-parse paths, so the HTTP route **and** the `get-session` MCP tool both receive it) and surfaced by a new `SessionMetaPanel` below the stats strip on the session detail page — git-activity chips, capability badges, and a tool-errors-by-category strip. Both readers reuse the `FileCache` mtime/size singleton (mirrors `claudeFacets.ts`). 11 new tests in `tests/claudeStats.test.ts` (temp-home isolation) cover well-formed parsing, the degrade-to-null-on-malformed contract for both files, defensive coercion of bad `dailyActivity` entries, snake→camel mapping, the `session_id` fallback, and cross-check drift math incl. divide-by-zero guards. Docs: `docs/help/stats.md` (cross-check card) + `docs/help/sessions.md` (session-metadata panel) + mirrors. No schema change. Review hardening (PR #184): the stats-cache mtime is folded into the `/api/stats` ETag (so a change to it alone can't 304 a stale cross-check), and when the sessions list is unavailable `crossCheck.observedMessages` is reported as `null` (the Messages row hides) rather than a misleading `0`.
- **Stuck-loop detection on the session Diagnosis tab (TODO: cc-blackbox-inspired).** A new `stuck-loop` quality finding flags runs of 3+ consecutive tool calls that repeat the **same** tool with **identical arguments AND identical result text** — the strongest "agent is not making progress" signal, distinct from the existing tool-failure streak (errors vary across turns) and the one-shot retry cycle (inputs change). New `detectStuckLoops` detector + `StuckLoopFinding` type in `src/lib/usage/sessionQuality.ts`, fused into the single-pass `computeSessionQuality` alongside the cache/compaction/failure-streak detectors (argument equality is order-independent via a sorted-key stable stringify; interleaved tool-less commentary turns do not break a run). Surfaces automatically in `DiagnosisPanel` via the shared `<FindingCard>` (no UI change needed — the panel renders findings generically), severity P1 (P0 at ≥5 repeats), and forces the session outcome to **stuck** in `sessionDiagnosis.ts`. Computed on demand from JSONL — no schema change or `DERIVED_VERSION` bump. False-positive guards (PR #183 review): a real human prompt between reruns barriers the run (user-driven reruns aren't the model looping), missing tool results stay `undefined` (so "no result" never matches "no result"), and results truncated at the 2 KB preview cap can't anchor a loop (different long outputs may share a prefix); whitespace-only-but-observed results still count. 12 tests covering the 3-repeat threshold, result/argument divergence, key-order independence, interleaved-commentary non-breaking, the human-prompt barrier, missing/truncated/whitespace results, fused-pass parity, and the diagnosis finding + outcome. Docs updated (`docs/help/sessions.md` + mirror): Diagnosis is now a 9-category analysis.
- **Hook payload typed-parser + background-activity portfolio surface (T2.3).** Two-part landing. T2.3a: new pure module `src/lib/hooks/payload.ts` (`parseHookPayload`, `HookPayload` discriminated union over 9 event variants) turns the raw JSON body Claude Code POSTs to `/api/hooks` into a typed shape per `hook_event_name`. Previously the route stored only the envelope (`session_id`, `cwd`, `tool_name`, `message`, `tool_response.is_error`) and the rest of the payload was thrown away. `HookEvent.payload?: HookPayload | null` is now persisted into the in-memory ring buffer alongside the envelope; existing consumers (`toolFailed`, awaiting-permission Notification path, `STOP_EVENTS`) are untouched — the field is purely additive. Parser returns `null` (never throws) when a variant's required field is missing; defensive helpers (`str`/`bool`/`num`/`arr`) drop type-mismatched fields to `undefined` rather than poisoning the typed shape. Captures: `PreToolUse`/`PostToolUse` tool_name + tool_input + tool_response + duration_ms; `UserPromptSubmit` prompt; `Notification` matcher (with `notification_type` fallback); `Stop` and `SubagentStop` stop_hook_active + `background_tasks` + `session_crons`; `SubagentStop` additionally agent_id + agent_type + agent_transcript_path + last_assistant_message; `PreCompact` trigger (narrowed to `"manual" | "auto"`) + custom_instructions; `SessionStart` source + model + agent_type; `SessionEnd` reason. T2.3b: new portfolio page at **/background** (added to the Sessions sidebar group between Sessions and Memory) lists every `background_tasks` and `session_crons` array recently observed across all projects, sourced from a new lib helper `getProjectBackgroundActivity(slug)` and exposed via new endpoint `GET /api/hooks/background-activity` that returns `{projects: [{slug, projectName, backgroundTasks, sessionCrons, lastObservedAt}], totals: {backgroundTasks, sessionCrons, projectsWithActivity}}`. Inner element shape is `unknown[]` because the public Claude Code hooks doc doesn't yet publish field names; the page renders whatever own-keys each element carries via defensive runtime narrowing, so future field additions don't break the page. Freshness is enforced on the read side: `getProjectBackgroundActivity` ignores Stop / SubagentStop events older than `STALE_EVICT_MS` (5 min) and treats an explicit `background_tasks: []` on the latest Stop as authoritative (a finished task clears prior state); pre-v2.1.145 Stops that omit both keys are treated as "no info" and skipped to keep prior data visible. Known limitation documented in `docs/help/hooks.md` + mirror: the ring buffer itself is count-capped at 50 entries per project and not time-evicted at write time — a long-running background task whose session hasn't fired a Stop in the last 5 min won't appear here (the badge "lies by omission") even though the OS process is still running. SQLite-backed retention is the planned follow-up. 17 new unit tests in `tests/hookPayload.test.ts` cover each variant's happy path, null-on-missing-required-field, the matcher-vs-notification_type fallback, `Stop` accepting payloads without `background_tasks` (pre-v2.1.145 compatibility), non-array `background_tasks`/`session_crons` dropping to `undefined` defensively, `PreCompact` trigger narrowing on unknown values, and the empty-prompt vs missing-prompt distinction.
- **PR-URL → session reverse-index on the project detail page (T2.2).** Each session row on a project's Sessions tab now shows a small `PR #N` chip when that session ran `gh pr create` and captured a returned URL. Clicking the chip filters the in-page list to sessions associated with that PR; a banner above the list shows the active filter (`Filtering to sessions that created <owner>/<repo>/pull/N`) with an "open the PR on GitHub" inline link and a clear-filter button. Extraction happens at session-ingest time via a new pure module `src/lib/usage/prExtractor.ts` (`extractPrsFromEntries`, `extractPrLinkFromText`, `PrLink`) — walks each session's `ConversationEntry[]` collecting assistant `tool_use` blocks with name `Bash` whose command matches `gh pr create` at a statement boundary (start, after `&&`/`||`/`;`, or newline), with quoted regions stripped first so `grep "gh pr create" docs/` and `echo "remember gh pr create"` no longer false-positive. Calls are matched to user `tool_result` blocks by `tool_use_id` (NOT positional ordering — Claude routinely runs Bash in parallel and the results stream back arbitrary order). The URL regex (`https?://github.com/<owner>/<repo>/pull/<N>\b`) anchors on `/pull/` so issues/discussions/commits never get misattributed, requires a trailing word boundary so `pull/42xyz` doesn't extract `42`, and rejects owner/repo segments containing no alphanumerics so `https://github.com/./../pull/5` is filtered out. When the result text contains multiple PR URLs (e.g., a `--body 'Closes #5'` echo precedes the new URL), the extractor prefers a URL that appears at the start of a line — matching gh CLI's canonical output shape — and falls back to the first match otherwise. `repo` is derived from the URL — NOT the session's git remote — because Claude can open PRs against forks or sibling repos. Per-session output is sorted by PR number ascending in both file-parse and DB read paths so chip order is stable across backends.

  New DB migration **v14** adds `session_prs (session_id, pr_url, pr_number, repo)` with composite PK and `FK ON DELETE CASCADE` to `sessions`; `INSERT OR IGNORE` semantics make repeated tail-appends and full reconciles idempotent. The write-time pipeline in `writeSession` saves the prior `session_prs` rows BEFORE the cascade DELETE and merges them with the fresh extraction on re-insert (with the fresh set winning on URL dedup), so a thrown extractor on a re-parse (returning `[]` via `safeExtractPrs`) can never silently destroy good PR data. `appendSessionTail` adds a fallback **straddle-recovery** pass: a cheap `hasOrphanToolResults` flag computed during tail parse triggers a full-file PR re-extract, which catches the case where a `gh pr create` Bash call lives in already-persisted bytes but its result lands in a later tail-append. Without this recovery, normal append-only file growth would have silently dropped these PRs until the next `DERIVED_VERSION` bump. Row counters use `result.changes` so `INSERT OR IGNORE` NOOPs don't inflate the indexer's soak-monitoring metric.

  Read path: `loadSessionsListFromDb` adds a single batched `SELECT ... FROM session_prs ORDER BY session_id, pr_number` to assemble `SessionSummary.prs?: PrLink[]` — no N+1. `/api/sessions` accepts a new `?pr=<url>` query param that filters sessions by exact URL match (and is included in the ETag salt so 304s stay correct across filter switches). The UI's PR chip is rendered as `<span role="button" tabIndex={0}>` (not `<button>`) so it's not an invalid interactive-content descendant of the row's `<Link>`; both `onClick` and `onKeyDown` (Enter/Space) call `setPrFilter` with `preventDefault` + `stopPropagation` so the parent link's navigation never fires.

  30 tests in `tests/prExtractor.test.ts` cover positional safety with interleaved tool calls, tool_result content shape (string vs. array of text blocks), multi-PR per session, dedup across multiple tool_use_ids, false-positive rejection (`gh issue create`, PR URLs in `git log` output, hyphenated near-misses like `gh-pr-create`, `gh pr create` inside quoted arguments, shell-commented invocations), URL edge cases (trailing slash, anchor, query string, repos with dots, `pull/42xyz` non-boundary, `./..` path-traversal-ish repos), line-isolated URL preference vs. embedded reference, fallback when no URL is line-isolated, HEREDOC-style multiline commands, chained-after-`&&` invocations, missing/malformed `tool_use_id`, and concatenated tool_result blocks under the same id. 4 new integration tests in `tests/dbIngest.test.ts` cover the parse → DB → read pipeline end-to-end: single PR write, multi-PR per session sorted ascending, preservation across a re-parse whose fresh extractor returns `[]`, and straddle recovery for a call/result pair split across an ingest cycle.
- **Projected context-cost chip on `/agents` and `/skills` rows + detail pages (T2.1).** Each catalog row and detail header now shows a muted-mono chip — e.g. `~1.2k · 0.6%` — estimating the token cost of injecting that agent/skill's body into the Claude Code context window. Renders only when the indexer captured a non-zero `fileBytes` for the entry; absent for orphan-usage rows (no catalog file behind them). Hover tooltip expands to the full breakdown: `~1,234 tokens · 0.62% of 200,000-token context window`. Mirrors the `/plugin` marketplace UX shipped in Claude Code v2.1.132 so users can pre-screen catalog weight before invocation. New util `src/lib/usage/tokenEstimate.ts` exports `bytesToTokens`, `contextWindowPercent`, `estimateTokensFromBytes`, `withProjectedContextCost`, `formatProjectedContextCost`, `formatTokenCount`, `formatContextWindowPercent`, and `BYTES_PER_TOKEN` / `DEFAULT_CONTEXT_WINDOW_TOKENS` constants — single source of truth for both the per-row chip and the portfolio overhead estimator (`src/lib/contextOverhead.ts` refactored to re-export `BYTES_PER_TOKEN` from the new util so the heuristic can never drift). `CatalogEntryBase.fileBytes` lifted from `SkillEntry` to the shared base so `AgentEntry` carries it too; `walkAgents.ts:makeAgentEntry` now captures `Buffer.byteLength(text, "utf-8")` at walk time when the body is already in memory (no extra fs.stat pass). `CatalogEntryBase.projectedContextCost` is a new optional field populated at the catalog API/MCP layer (not the indexer — so the context-window denominator can later come from the active model). Percent column is computed against a fixed 200k-token window — the Claude Sonnet 4.6 / Opus 4.7 (non-1M) default — and is intentionally a ceiling estimate for skills (per existing `/stats` model: full body weight on invocation, not the frontmatter-only always-on cost). Tiny shares floor at `<0.1%` to keep visually-misleading `0.0%` off the chip. **MCP surface:** the four catalog tools (`list-agents`, `get-agent`, `list-skills`, `get-skill`) now include `projectedContextCost` on every entry so a connected Claude Code agent can self-inspect which catalog items will dominate its working context before invoking them. **REST surface:** `/api/agents`, `/api/agents/[id]`, `/api/skills`, `/api/skills/[id]` all include the field too — UI is now a single-source-of-truth consumer (server computes, client formats via `formatProjectedContextCost`) instead of duplicating the compute in each browser component. 23 new tests in `tests/tokenEstimate.test.ts` covering byte-count edge cases (zero/negative/NaN/Infinity), token-format thresholds (sub-1k literal, 1k–100k `.1k`, ≥100k whole-`k`), percent formatting (`<0.1%` floor, sub-10% one-decimal, ≥10% whole-percent), the `estimateTokensFromBytes` triple including chip-label composition, and the `withProjectedContextCost` enricher (returns input unchanged on missing/zero-token bytes, populates the field for real bodies, preserves all other fields, non-mutating, honors custom context windows).
- **MCP test-suite timeouts (#158) — explicit per-call SDK timeouts.** Four MCP tests intermittently failed (and sometimes consistently failed) with `MCP error -32001: Request timed out` from `@modelcontextprotocol/sdk` because the SDK's `DEFAULT_REQUEST_TIMEOUT_MSEC = 60_000` fired before the slower lib functions completed: `client.listResources()` in `mcpServer.test.ts` invokes every registered resource template's `list` callback (enumerating sessions etc. — slow on a machine with hundreds of indexed sessions); `list-projects` cold-scans `C:\dev\*`; `minder://stats` aggregates every session JSONL when the SQLite index isn't enabled; `minder://usage/7d` and `get-usage-by-day` do the same. Vitest test-level timeouts were already bumped to 90s but the SDK's per-request layer bailed earlier. Fix: pass `{ timeout: 120_000 }` as the SDK `RequestOptions` argument on the five affected calls. Per-test budgets also bumped to 120_000 to match. Net effect: 2 → 0 pre-existing test failures, 6 → 1 skipped (the previously-skipped 5 are siblings of the boot-suite's failed `beforeAll`, now passing alongside it). Unblocks the local pre-commit hook for all future PRs.
- **Detail-page route — pre-existing #165 (decode params at boundary).** `src/app/agents/[id]/page.tsx` and `src/app/skills/[id]/page.tsx` now `decodeURIComponent` the dynamic `params.id` before passing to the DetailView. Background: Next.js 16 returns `params.id` as the URL-encoded form (`agent%3Aplugin%3Afoo%3Abar`) rather than decoded. `AgentDetailView` / `SkillDetailView` then called `encodeURIComponent(id)` when building the API fetch URL, producing a double-encoded path (`%253A...`) that always 404'd. Effect: `/agents/[id]` and `/skills/[id]` rendered "not found" for every catalog item — including via clickthrough from the browsers — and **the T2.1 detail-page chip was unreachable** until this fix. Both pages now use a defensive `safeDecode` wrapper (catches malformed URI throws and falls back to the raw id). Discovered during T2.1 visual verification; filed as #165 and fixed in the same PR. Verified visually: `/agents/agent:plugin:feature-dev:code-reviewer` now renders, `context: ~749 · 0.4%` MetaPill visible; `/skills/skill:user:user:agent_prompt_guide` renders with `context: ~3.1k · 1.6%`.
- **Per-agent runtime metrics in Session Subagents tab (T1.2 — OTEL path).** Each subagent card on `/sessions/<id>` now shows cost (USD), token count, model name, and duration alongside the existing top-5 tool usage. `SubagentInfo` gains optional `costUsd`, `inputTokens`, `outputTokens`, `cacheReadTokens`, `cacheCreateTokens`, `model`, `durationMs`, `firstTimestamp`, `lastTimestamp` fields populated by a new `enrichSubagentsFromOtel` step that queries the `otel_events` table for `subagent_completed` events (per-invocation metadata: agent_type, prompt.id, duration_ms, model, total_tokens) and rolls up matching `api_request` events by `prompt.id` for exact `cost_usd` + I/O token split. JSONL Agent dispatches are matched chronologically to OTEL completions per agent_type (n-th JSONL dispatch ↔ n-th OTEL completion). The enrichment is best-effort — when the SQLite driver isn't loaded or the session has no OTEL coverage, the subagent skeleton (type, description) still renders without runtime chips. Wired into both `scanSessionDetail` and `loadSessionDetailFromDb`, so the production DB-mode path shows the metrics. Two-paragraph context: T1.2's original plan called for `agent_id`/`parent_agent_id` on OTEL `claude_code.tool` spans (v2.1.145), but DB probes of v2.1.150 traffic confirmed those attrs never shipped. A JSONL-based fallback was attempted first but JSONL `isSidechain` data is now empty in 100% of sessions (probed 2026-05-25: 0/214) — the same change has also silently zeroed the per-agent cost column on `/agents` (tracked as a separate P1 bug). OTEL `subagent_completed` is the only working data source today. 5 new tests in `tests/subagentMetrics.test.ts` covering chronological matching, excess JSONL dispatches, no-OTEL fallback, and api_request rollup. `loadSessionDetailFromDb` becomes async (callers updated via TS signature change).
- **`claude agents --json` liveness ground-truth — data layer + ProjectCard surfacing (T1.1).** Project Minder now shells out to `claude agents --json` (v2.1.145+) and merges live-process identity into the JSONL-mtime liveness payload. `LiveSession` gains four optional fields: `pid`, `isLive` (`true` = CLI confirms process alive, `false` = CLI ran but session not in live list, `undefined` = CLI unavailable), `processStartedAt`, and `processName` (set when a `claude agents` session was dispatched with `--name`). `StatusPayload` gains `cliAvailable: boolean` so consumers can tell "no live sessions" from "CLI broken." New module `src/lib/claudeAgentsCli.ts` wraps the CLI with 5s timeout, 10s `globalThis` cache, dedupe of concurrent in-flight calls, and a `null`-vs-`[]` return contract that distinguishes "CLI broken/old version" from "CLI healthy, zero sessions" so the merge applies only when trustworthy. `/api/pulse` (and `PulseSnapshot`) gain `verifiedLiveSlugs`, `liveProcessInfo: Record<slug, {pid, name?}>`, and `cliAvailable`; when the CLI is unavailable, `verifiedLiveSlugs` falls back to the existing hook-server `liveSlugs` so dashboards on older Claude Code versions render unchanged. **ProjectCard's `LiveStatusBadge` becomes three-tier:** (1) `awaiting` → existing amber input badge (highest priority); (2) `verifiedLive` (CLI confirms PID alive) → existing solid green "live" badge with PID and optional session name in the tooltip; (3) `liveSlugs ∖ verifiedLiveSlugs` (hook events claim live but CLI says no live PID) → new dim outlined "live?" badge that flags stale ring-buffer entries from crashed sessions. 10 new tests in `tests/claudeAgentsCli.test.ts`.
- **ClaudeLint — browser lint badges, /stats aggregate, vendored rules (Wave F).** Per-target lint badges on the `/agents`, `/skills`, `/commands`, and `/plugins` browsers — each row shows a severity-tinted count chip (`LintCountChip`) that links to the project's Config Lint tab. New `useLintFindings` hook fetches `/api/projects` once and indexes findings by file path. New vendored rule modules for skills (`skill/missing-description` P1, `skill/long-description` P2), agents (`agent/missing-description` P1, `agent/long-description` P2), and commands (`command/missing-description` P1), plus cross-scope duplicate-name/slug rules. Global catalog-lint pass (`src/lib/scanner/catalogLint.ts`) runs once per scan over user + plugin scope entries; cross-scope duplicate detection runs over the full catalog. `/stats` page gains a "Config Lint" section with P0/P1/P2 severity counts, projects-affected count, and a by-target bar chart. `ProjectDetail` now syncs the active tab to a `?tab=` URL query parameter, enabling deep-links to `/project/<slug>?tab=config-lint`. 6 new integration tests in `tests/scannerCatalogLint.test.ts`.
- **ClaudeLint — workspace config lint pipeline (Wave E — core UI).** Adds `ConfigLintPanel` component that renders a `LintReport` grouped by target (CLAUDE.md, Skills, Agents, Commands, Settings, Hooks, MCP Servers, Plugins, Output Styles, LSP Config), then by severity (P0/P1/P2) within each group. - **ClaudeLint — workspace config lint pipeline (Wave D).** Two new scanner modules: `src/lib/scanner/outputStyles.ts` reads `.claude/output-styles/<name>/PROMPT.md` (and any `.md` file) per subdirectory, parsing frontmatter via `parseFrontmatter`; returns `OutputStylesInfo` with `styles[]`. `src/lib/scanner/lspConfig.ts` reads `.claude/lsp.json` via `tryParseJsonc`, tolerates JSONC comments, returns `LspConfigInfo`. - **ClaudeLint — workspace config lint pipeline (Wave C).** Two vendored rule modules: `src/lib/lint/rules/hooks.ts` flags hook entries missing a `timeout` command (`hook/no-timeout` P2) and duplicate event handlers with the same source+event+matcher tuple (`hook/duplicate-event-handler` P2). `src/lib/lint/rules/plugins.ts` flags enabled-but-blocked plugins (`plugin/blocked-but-enabled` P1) and enabled plugins without a version pin or git SHA (`plugin/unpinned-version` P2). `runConfigLint` orchestrator extended to merge user-scope hooks from `getUserConfig()` with project-scope hooks before linting, and to pass the user-scope plugin list. 10 new tests across `tests/lintRulesHooks.test.ts` and `tests/lintRulesPlugins.test.ts`. `hooksPromise` hoisted in the scanner to share one scan between the main pipeline and configLint inputs.
- **ClaudeLint — workspace config lint pipeline (Wave B).** Wires the `claude-code-lint` library CLI (`check-all --format json`) as the library lint pass: spawns the CLI as a subprocess per project, parses structured JSON output, maps validator findings to `LintFinding` with P1/P2 severity and `docsUrl` links. Engine-error fence captures spawn/parse failures in `LintReport.engineErrors` without crashing the scan. - **ClaudeLint — workspace config lint pipeline (Wave A).** Foundation for a workspace-wide config audit across ten Claude Code surfaces (CLAUDE.md, skills, agents, commands, settings, hooks, MCPs, plugins, output styles, LSPs). Wave A ships the types (`LintFinding`, `LintTarget`, `LintEngine`, `LintReport`), engine skeleton with a three-pass architecture (adapter / library / vendored), deduplicate logic (library > vendored > adapter priority by rule-family key), and a CLAUDE.md adapter that re-emits existing audit findings into the unified shape without duplicating rules. Wired into the scanner as a `configLint` field on `ProjectData`, gated behind a new `configLint` feature flag (default-off). 22 new tests in `tests/lintAdapterClaudeMd.test.ts` and `tests/lintEngine.test.ts`.
- **Claude status alerts.** Project Minder now polls `status.claude.com/api/v2/summary.json` and surfaces active Claude incidents in a sticky banner below the topbar on every route, plus toast notifications when an incident appears, transitions status, or resolves.
