(5) `POST /api/scan` now calls `invalidateLiveStatusCache()` and `invalidateClaudeAgentsCache()` alongside the other six cache invalidations, so manual rescans no longer serve stale process listings for up to 10 s. Three new tests cover the typeguard's non-finite rejection and the negative-result TTL with fake timers.
- **Home Live activity card read "(no prompt)" for every session.** Real Claude Code JSONL stores HUMAN-typed user turns with `message.content` as a **string** (e.g. `"fix the build please"`), while assistant turns and tool-result turns use arrays of typed blocks. The DB-ingest pipeline in `src/lib/db/ingest.ts:666` ran `extractText()` from `@/lib/usage/contentBlocks` on whatever `message.content` happened to be — and `extractText()` is intentionally array-only (its docstring says it walks `{type, text}` block lists). For string content it short-circuits to `""`, which meant `userText === ""`, so `isHumanText(userText)` was false, so the `initial_prompt` / `last_prompt` assignment block at lines 670-676 never ran. Every real session in the SQLite index ended up with NULL prompt columns, and `/api/sessions` responded with neither `initialPrompt` nor `lastPrompt` (the fields are optional in `SessionSummary`, so `JSON.stringify` dropped them entirely). Home read `s.lastPrompt?.slice(0, 60) || s.initialPrompt?.slice(0, 60) || "(no prompt)"` and fell through to the empty-state literal for every row. `searchableText` masked the problem because the search-index accumulator IS fed from assistant array content, so the field looked populated even though it never contained the user prompt that anchors the session's identity. File-parse path was unaffected (it uses its own `extractHumanText()` which handles strings). Fix at the DB-ingest call site adds a `typeof textSource === "string" ? textSource : extractText(textSource)` branch — keeps `extractText()`'s array-walking semantics for callers that pass typed block arrays (the documented intent of the helper) and handles the string shape exactly at the user-turn site where Claude Code legitimately emits it. New regression test in `tests/dbIngest.test.ts` builds a session with raw-string `message.content` for two user turns and asserts `initial_prompt` / `last_prompt` land on the row; the pre-existing array-content path is still exercised by the other 24 ingest tests. **Note for existing installs:** the SQLite index keys ingest off JSONL file mtime, so already-indexed sessions stay with NULL prompts until their JSONL file changes (which happens naturally as Claude Code appends new turns to active sessions). To populate prompts for old idle sessions, delete `~/.minder/index.db*` and restart the dev server — the indexer rebuilds from JSONL with the fixed extractor.
- **OTEL receivers bypassed the DB state machine and 500-ed on EBUSY.** Both `src/app/api/otel/v1/metrics/route.ts` and `src/app/api/otel/v1/logs/route.ts` had their own `let initPromise: Promise<…> | null = null` and called `initDb()` from `@/lib/db/migrations` directly. That path is the raw migration runner — no retry, no transient-error classification, no quarantine cap. When the indexer worker held the SQLite file open and an OTEL POST arrived, `getDb()` threw on `new Database(DB_PATH)`, `initDb()` interpreted it as corruption, `quarantineCorruptDb()` tried to `fs.rename(index.db, index.db.corrupt-*)`, the rename hit EBUSY because the file was still locked by the indexer's live handle, the fallback `fs.rm` failed for the same reason, and the original EBUSY rebubbled through `ensureReady` into Next's error path as a 500. Replaced both routes' `initPromise` shim with `ensureSchemaReady()` from `@/lib/data` (a previously-internal helper now exported) — the state-machine path that already classifies EBUSY / EPERM / ENOENT / ENOTEMPTY / SQLITE_BUSY / SQLITE_LOCKED as transient, retries with `[100, 300, 900]ms` backoff (`src/lib/data/index.ts:130,148-155`), caches `transient-failed` for 30 s, and caps quarantines at 2 cumulative runs before going `permanent-failed`. **Why `ensureSchemaReady()` rather than `probeInitStatus()`:** the latter intentionally short-circuits when `MINDER_USE_DB=0` so `/api/health` reports `idle` instead of actively probing (correct for a passive health surface), but OTEL is write-side and needs the DB regardless of which read-path backend is selected — using `probeInitStatus()` here would 503 every OTEL POST under `MINDER_USE_DB=0` (Copilot PR #117 P2 regression). Effect: a momentary file lock now returns 503 ("OTEL storage not available") instead of 500, and lock contentions enter the state machine so Home can observe them.
- **Hydration mismatch on the topbar bell badge.** `AppTopbar` consumes `usePulse()` for the notifications-button `title` and badge-dot, both of which depend on `snapshot.approvalCount + snapshot.pendingSteps`. In dev mode the `/api/pulse` poll can resolve before hydration completes (e.g. while React is still hydrating the SSR HTML), which fires a `setSnapshot` with real counts (242 pending steps in the reported repro) and triggers `Hydration failed because the server rendered HTML didn't match the client` — the SSR frame had `title="No new notifications"` with no badge, the post-poll frame had `title="242 pending — open Status"` with a `<span className="badge-dot">`. Fix mirrors the existing `hydrated` flag pattern in `AppSidebar.tsx:138-139` (originally introduced for HIGH-4 in the 2026-05-10 review): `AppTopbar` now gates `totalAlerts` on a post-mount `hydrated` state so the first client frame always reports zero alerts and matches the SSR HTML; the poll-derived value swaps in on the next render after `useEffect` flushes.
- **CLAUDE.md audit no longer claims Claude Code truncates at 200 lines.** The original Wave 2.2 audit shipped with a `visibility-cap` finding whose title literally said "only first 200 are loaded by Claude Code" and whose penalty formula `(100 − visibility%) × 0.5` assumed a hard truncation. There is no such truncation — Claude Code reads the whole file. The 150–200 line guidance is a practitioner heuristic for *instruction-following* (rule adherence drops as the file grows; latency rises; the file competes with code/errors for working memory) and 40 KB is Claude Code's own warning threshold for re-injection-per-turn cost. Replaced `visibility-cap` with a tiered `long-index` finding (>150 → P2 −3, >300 → P1 −8, >500 → P0 −15) and retiered `file-size` (>40 KB → P1 −10, >80 KB → P0 −20). `long-index` is now scoped to the project's own CLAUDE.md (post-`@import`-expand), not combined with `~/.claude/CLAUDE.md` — a bloated user-scope file shouldn't drag every project's score down. The dashboard sub-line and help docs no longer claim a hard cap. `ClaudeMdAuditCode` union and `ClaudeMdAuditInfo` interface adjusted: `"visibility-cap"` removed, `"long-index"` added; `visibleLines` removed; `projectLines` added. Tests rewritten: 5 cases now cover the long-index/file-size tiers (was 1 + 1 case). The historical Wave 2.2 entry below describes the shipped behavior at release time and is preserved unchanged for traceability.

### Security
- `~/.minder/secrets.json` written with mode `0o600` on POSIX. On Windows, file inherits the `~/.minder/` directory NTFS ACL; manual `icacls` hardening documented in help/terminal.md.
- Telegram bot token moved from public config to `secrets.json` exclusively (was a Wave-1 placeholder; no setter existed before this wave).
- **Wave 6.2 — Cluster O + G remainder: 5 D3 visualizations.** TODOs #207, #209, #211, #212, #213.
  - **Concurrency Timeline (#207).** New "Concurrency" tab on session detail (visible when session has subagents). Gantt-style horizontal bars showing main agent + each subagent over session duration. Bar width = active time span; falls back to turn-index proportions when wall-clock timestamps are missing. `GET /api/sessions/[sessionId]/concurrency-timeline` (60s cache).
  - **Error Propagation Map (#209).** New "Errors" tab on project detail (visible when project has sessions). Cross-session bar chart of error rates by subagent hierarchy depth (red → purple gradient), top error-prone agents, and tool error breakdown. `GET /api/projects/[slug]/error-propagation` (5-min cache + mtime key).
  - **Model Delegation Flow (#211).** New "Delegation" tab on session detail (visible when session has subagents). Two-column Bezier flow diagram: primary models (left) → subagent models (right). Curve thickness = delegation count; curve opacity = token volume. `GET /api/sessions/[sessionId]/model-delegation` (60s cache).
  - **Agent Network Graph (#213).** New "Network" tab on session detail (visible when session has subagents). D3 force-directed graph of agent communication. Node radius = message volume; directed arrows = delegation edges. `GET /api/sessions/[sessionId]/agent-network` (60s cache).
  - **File Coupling Arc (#212).** Replaces bar list in the Hot Files panel "File Coupling" section when ≥4 unique files are present. Arc diagram with files on a horizontal axis, quadratic Bezier arcs for co-edited pairs (opacity = coupling strength, thickness = co-occurrence count). Click a file node to highlight incident arcs.
  - New shared palette `agentPalette.ts` (8-color + depth gradient + model family colors) and `relPath.ts` helper extracted for viz reuse.
- **Wave 6.1 — Cluster N: D3 Visualizations.** TODOs #201, #203, #205.

  - **Orchestration DAG (#201).** New "Orchestration" tab on session detail pages (visible when `subagentCount > 0`). D3 hierarchy tree showing parent→child subagent delegation, colored by agent type. Computed on demand from JSONL via `GET /api/sessions/[sessionId]/orchestration` (60s cache).
  - **Tool Execution Flow — Sankey (#203).** Portfolio-wide tool transition Sankey on `/usage`. Shows the most common tool→tool sequences with top-N slider (5–30). Self-loop repetitions (same tool consecutively) shown as `×N` badge instead of a self-referential edge (d3-sankey limitation). Data from new `computeToolTransitions()` in `aggregator.ts`.
  - **Session Complexity scatter (#205).** Three-preset scatter plot on `/stats`. Presets: Complexity vs Cost, Context Pressure, Reliability. Log-scale toggles. Click a dot to navigate to session detail.
- `d3`, `d3-sankey`, `@types/d3`, `@types/d3-sankey` added as dependencies.
- **Wave 5.3 — Cluster M: Toggle UX.** TODOs #39, #54, #55 from `~/.claude/plans/our-to-do-list-has-gentle-cookie.md`. TODO #40 (hook enable/disable) deferred — see Notes below.
  - **Skill enable/disable toggle (#39).** User-scope skills can be toggled from the `/skills` browser. Toggle moves the skill directory (or `.md` file for standalone layout) between `~/.claude/skills/` and `~/.claude/skills-disabled/`. Claude Code's live change detection picks up the removal/restoration within the active session without restart. Disabled rows are shown at 55% opacity with an amber "disabled" badge. New `src/lib/skillToggle.ts` + `POST /api/skills/[id]/toggle`. Walker (`walkSkills.ts`) now traverses both roots in parallel and tags disabled entries.
  - **MCP server enable/disable toggle (#55).** Project-scope MCP servers can be toggled from the Config browser's MCP tab. Toggle writes `disabledMcpjsonServers` to `.claude/settings.local.json` (gitignored, personal preference — teammates unaffected). Non-project-scope servers (user/desktop/managed/plugin) show a tooltip explaining why the toggle is absent. New `src/lib/mcpToggle.ts` + `POST /api/projects/[slug]/mcp-toggle`. Scanner reads `disabledMcpjsonServers` from both `settings.local.json` and `settings.json` and tags servers accordingly.
  - **Effective config view (#54).** New "effective view" toggle in the Config browser (MCP and Hooks tabs). When on, each row shows a state badge (`active` / `shadowed` / `disabled` / `conflict`) computed client-side from the full server/hook list. MCP logic: `managed` scope is exclusive (all others shadowed); duplicate server names across scopes → `conflict`; `disabled` flag wins. Hook logic: same key appearing in multiple scopes → `conflict` (hooks are additive in Claude Code, not shadowed). Pure client-side `useMemo` computation — no new endpoints. New `src/lib/effectiveConfig.ts`.

### Internal

  - 8-pass deobfuscation pipeline (`stripZeroWidth`, `stripTagChars`, `stripVariationSelectors`, `stripBidiControls`, `stripHtmlComments`, `normalizeUnicode`, `decodeBase64Blocks`, `unescapeSequences` + optional leetspeak pass).

  - Help doc at `/config?type=mcp`.

- **Wave 10.2b — Cluster X (part 2): Codex CLI adapter.** TODO #219.
  - New `src/lib/adapters/codex.ts`: `discover()` recursively walks `~/.codex/sessions/` and `~/.codex/archived_sessions/`, deduping sessions by ID. `parseFile()` translates Codex's event-stream JSONL format (session_meta / turn_context / response_item / event_msg) into `UsageTurn[]`.
  - Token delta math: prefers `last_token_usage` per turn; falls back to delta from `total_token_usage` when absent. `cacheReadTokens = min(cached_input_tokens, input_tokens)`; `cacheCreateTokens` is always 0 (Codex does not report cache creation).
  - Project slug derived from `cwd` in session metadata via `encodeProjectPath` + `toSlug` — same encoding used by the scanner, so Codex sessions correlate with the correct project in analytics.
  - Help doc updated: Codex adapter status changed from "Coming" to "Active"; Codex-specific section added.
- **Wave 10.2c — Cluster X (part 3): Gemini CLI adapter.** TODO #221.
  - New `src/lib/adapters/gemini.ts`: `discover()` walks `~/.gemini/tmp/<project>/chats/session-*.json`. Project folder paths resolved from `~/.gemini/projects.json` (primary) or `.project_root` files (fallback for hashed-directory layouts used by newer Gemini CLI versions). `parseFile()` parses Gemini's JSON session format (user / gemini / info messages) into `UsageTurn[]`.
  - Token math: per-turn deltas directly from `tokens.{input, output, cached}` on each gemini message. `cacheReadTokens = min(cached, input)`; `cacheCreateTokens` is always 0.
  - Thoughts and tool calls extracted and included in assistant turn text and `toolCalls` array.
  - `GEMINI_HOME` environment variable overrides `~/.gemini/` for custom installs.
  - Help doc updated: Gemini CLI adapter status changed from "Coming" to "Active"; Gemini-specific section added.
- **Wave 10.1c — Cluster W (part 3): Multi-agent swarm dispatch.** TODO #247.
  - New `ops_swarms` table (migration v5) with `name`, `mode` (`worktree`|`shared`), `project_path`, `status`, `completed_at`. Two new nullable columns on `ops_tasks`: `swarm_id` (FK → `ops_swarms`) and `swarm_role` (`member`|`coordinator`), added via `ALTER TABLE ADD COLUMN` — zero migration cost for existing rows.
  - **Swarm creation**: `createSwarm()` — single SQLite transaction creates the swarm row + 2–8 member tasks (with `worktreePath`/`projectPath` in metadata for worktree mode) + optional coordinator task with `task_dependencies` edges to every member.
  - **Coordinator "all-terminal" SQL guard**: `claimPendingTask` and `promoteApprovalTasks` use a role-aware `NOT EXISTS` subquery — non-coordinator tasks need blockers `= 'done'`; coordinator tasks unblock when all blockers reach any terminal state (`done`|`failed`|`cancelled`).
  - **Coordinator context injection**: `updateSwarmStatus()` appends member `output_summary` values to the coordinator task's `description` field when all members become terminal — injected exactly once (guarded by `<!-- swarm-summaries-injected -->` marker) so the coordinator runs with full context of what each member produced.
  - **Worktree spawner**: `runWorktreeTask()` — calls `git worktree add -B <branch> <path> HEAD` via `execFile` (not shell exec), sets `cwd` to the worktree directory via a `spawnFn` closure (no signature change to `runClassicTask`/`runStreamTask`). Worktree paths are siblings of the project dir using `--claude-worktrees-` naming (compatible with the existing worktrees scanner).
  - **Dispatcher routing**: detects worktree tasks by `worktreePath` in metadata; routes to `runWorktreeTask`; calls `updateSwarmStatus(swarmId)` after every swarm task completes/fails.
  - **REST surface**: `GET/POST /api/swarms`, `GET /api/swarms/[id]`, `DELETE /api/swarms/[id]/worktrees` (idempotent `git worktree remove --force` cleanup).
  - **SwarmComposer modal** — name, project path (prefilled from project card or text input on Tasks page), mode radio, 2–8 member definitions, optional coordinator. Navigates to `/swarms/<id>` on success.
  - **Entry points**: "Launch Swarm" button on Tasks page; "Launch Swarm…" in the project card dropdown (pre-fills project path).
  - **Swarms nav entry** added to Mission Control group in AppNav.
  - **`/swarms`** — list page with status dot and mode badges. **`/swarms/[id]`** — detail page polling every 5 s while running; shows per-member status/cost/session link, total cost, "Remove worktrees" action for worktree-mode swarms.
- **Wave 10.1b — Cluster W (part 2): Task dependency graph.** TODO #167.
  - New `task_dependencies(task_id, blocker_id)` table (migration v4) with `CHECK (task_id != blocker_id)`, `UNIQUE (task_id, blocker_id)`, and cascade-delete. Indexed on both columns.
  - **Dispatcher SQL guard**: `claimPendingTask` and `promoteApprovalTasks` skip tasks whose blockers haven't reached `done` via a single `NOT EXISTS (...)` subquery — atomically safe, no JS-level filter.
  - **Cycle prevention at insert time**: DFS from `taskId` over downstream edges before each insert; throws `CycleError` (409) if `blockerId` is reachable, preventing cyclic graphs.
  - `addDependency(taskId, blockerId)` — idempotent (ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING); `removeDependency(taskId, blockerId)` — idempotent 204; `listDependencies(taskId)` — `{ blockedBy, blocks }`; `listAllDependencies()` — full table scan for kanban+DAG+Gantt.
  - New REST surface: `GET/POST /api/tasks/[id]/dependencies`, `DELETE /api/tasks/[id]/dependencies/[blockerId]`.
  - `GET /api/kanban` now fetches all dependency edges and builds `blockedByMap`/`blocksMap` passed into `buildBoard`; task cards carry `blockedBy: number[]` and `blocks: number[]`.
  - **Blocked badge** on Kanban task cards when `blockedBy.length > 0` — gray chip with count.
  - **Three Kanban view modes** (Board / Dag / Gantt) via toolbar toggle; mode persisted to `localStorage` under `minder:kanban:view-mode`.
  - **Dag view** — `TaskDependencyGraph.tsx`: manual Sugiyama-style layered layout (`dependencyLayout.ts`), D3 SVG rendering, cubic Bezier edges with arrowhead marker, nodes colored by status, click → `/tasks?focus=<id>`. No new npm dependencies.
  - **Gantt view** — `TaskGanttChart.tsx`: `d3.scaleTime()` horizontal bars, one row per task ordered by layer, dependency arrows as dashed polylines, placeholder bars for pending/awaiting-approval tasks.
  - `dependencyLayout.ts` shared pure function (longest-path layer assignment + priority sort) used by both DAG and Gantt.
  - **Task Composer** gains a "Depends on (optional)" checkbox list of active tasks; creates dependency edges atomically with the task.
  - Help doc at `/kanban` updated with view modes and dependency semantics.
  - 32 new tests: `taskDependencies` (store), `dependencyLayout` (pure layout), `apiTaskDependencies` (route), plus extensions to `buildBoard` and `apiKanban`. 1656 tests pass, typecheck clean.

  - New `/kanban` page with a 5-column board (Working / Waiting / Idle / Done / Error) that unifies Claude Code sessions and dispatcher tasks in a single view.

- **Wave 9.2 — Cluster V: HITL decision queue, emergency stop, and todo delegation.** TODOs #245, #246, #248.
  - **#245 HITL decision queue.** Stream-mode sessions emit `DECISION: <prompt> [choices]` and `INBOX: <message>` markers on stdout; the dispatcher parses them via a new fence-aware `decisionParser.ts` and records them in a new `task_decisions` table (schema v2). Pending decisions surface in a new `DecisionsPanel` component on the dashboard; choosing an option writes the answer back to the child's stdin pipe. Inbox messages appear in a new `InboxPanel` scrollable feed. The spawner now opens stdin in pipe mode and maintains a `Map<taskId, ChildProcess>` (`getStreamChild` / `listStreamChildren`) for downstream stdin writes. New store helpers: `recordDecision`, `decideTask`, `listOpenDecisions`, `listInbox`, `countNewDecisions`. New API routes: `POST /api/tasks/[id]/decide`, `GET /api/decisions`, `GET /api/inbox`. `PulseSnapshot` extended with `decisionCount`, `inboxCount`, `dispatcherPaused`. Decision badge (`⏸ N waiting`) on TasksBrowser rows.
  - **#246 Emergency stop.** New `emergencyStop.ts` module walks `~/.minder/pids/`, verifies each PID via `tasklist /FI` (Windows) or `ps -p` (POSIX) against the string `claude`, and calls `killProcessTree(pid)` only for confirmed dispatcher children. Unconfirmed PIDs counted as `interactiveSpared` and left alone. Sets `emergencyStop: true` in `.minder.json` atomically. Dispatcher `tick()` checks the flag at the top of each loop and skips claim/spawn when paused. New `EmergencyStopButton` component in the dashboard header: red "Stop" with confirm dialog, flips to green "Resume" when paused. New API routes: `POST /api/tasks/emergency-stop`, `POST /api/tasks/emergency-stop/resume`.
  - **#248 TODO delegation.** New `todoDelegation.ts` module: `delegateTodo()` creates an `ops_tasks` row with `quadrant = "delegated-todo"` and `metadata = { sourceFile, lineNumber, projectSlug }`; `onTaskCompleteToggleTodo()` calls `todoWriter.toggleTodoInFile` on completion (best-effort, failure logged but does not fail the task). Schema v2 migration rebuilds `ops_tasks` to add `'delegated-todo'` to the quadrant CHECK constraint (SQLite cannot ALTER constraints in place) and a new `metadata TEXT` column. New API route: `POST /api/projects/[slug]/todos/delegate`. `TodoList` component gains a "Delegate" icon-button on each unchecked item (visible when `taskDispatcher` flag is on). `TasksBrowser` gains a "From TODOs" source filter (`quadrant = delegated-todo`).
  - 12 new `decisionParser` tests, 6 new `spawnerStdin` tests, 6 new `emergencyStop` tests, 8 new `todoDelegation` tests, 7 new `tasksDbV2` migration tests. 1587 tests pass, typecheck clean.
- **Wave 9.1c — Stream mode spawning.** `execution_mode: "stream"` tasks now use `claude -p --output-format stream-json --verbose` instead of `--output-format text`. NDJSON events are parsed from stdout: the `init` event writes `session_id` to the task row mid-run via a new `setSessionId()` store helper; the `result` event captures output text and `total_cost_usd`. Chunk-boundary safety is guaranteed by a line buffer that accumulates across `data` events with UTF-8 stream encoding. Non-JSON lines (hook output, warnings) are silently skipped. Task Composer now exposes an "Execution mode" selector (Classic / Stream). Dispatcher routes tasks by `execution_mode` field. 7 new `runStreamTask` tests.
- **Wave 9.1b — Cluster U (continued): Dispatcher loop + classic spawning + Task Composer.** TODO #244.
  - Dispatcher loop singleton (`globalThis.__minderDispatcher`) starts automatically on the first `/api/tasks` request. 30-second tick: writes heartbeat to `~/.minder/dispatcher-heartbeat.json`, materializes due cron schedules into `ops_tasks` rows (serialized transaction), promotes `requires_approval` tasks to `awaiting_approval`, claims up to 3 pending tasks and spawns `claude -p` (classic mode).
  - PID marker files at `~/.minder/pids/<pid>` — written on spawn, deleted on exit. `sweepStalePids()` on each tick cleans dead files via `process.kill(pid, 0)` (cross-platform, throws ESRCH if dead).
  - `POST /api/tasks/[id]/approve` — transitions `awaiting_approval → pending`, sets `approved_at`; dispatcher picks up on next tick.
  - `POST /api/tasks/[id]/rerun` — resets `failed` task to `pending`, clears all output fields (`error_message`, `started_at`, `completed_at`, `duration_ms`, `cost_usd`, `output_summary`, `session_id`).
  - Task Composer modal (`TaskComposer.tsx`) — "New task" button in TasksBrowser toolbar opens a full-form overlay. Fields: title, description, quadrant, priority, skill, model, risk level, scheduled_for, requires_approval, dry_run. POSTs to `/api/tasks` and refreshes the list on success.
  - New store helpers: `approveTask()`, `rerunTask()`, `completeTask()`, `failTask()`, `promoteApprovalTasks()`, `materializeSchedules()`.
  - `taskDispatcher` feature flag flipped to `wired: true`. Settings UI now shows it as active.
  - Help doc at `/help/tasks` updated with dispatcher architecture, approve/rerun usage, and upcoming Wave 9.1c (stream mode) and Wave 9.2 (HITL) roadmap.
  - Stream mode (line-buffered JSON, `session_id` extraction), `DECISION:` / `INBOX:` parsing, and emergency-stop button deferred to Wave 9.1c / 9.2.

Reads the OAuth access token from `~/.claude/.credentials.json` and makes a minimal POST to `api.anthropic.com/v1/messages` (Claude Haiku 4.5, 1 token, ~$0.00001/probe) to read `anthropic-ratelimit-unified-*` response headers. Reinstall button appears when the registered URL differs from the current origin. Per-channel awaiting-permission alert toggles.

"Re-distill" regenerates on demand. Reuses the same secretsStore + autoTitle LLM pattern.
  - **Markdown export (#233).** "Export" button opens a modal with section checkboxes (Conversation timeline, File operations, Subagents) and an optional turn-limit input. Client-side Markdown generation triggers a `.md` download via `URL.createObjectURL`; no new API route needed.
  - **Schema v8.** `sessions.starred_at TEXT`, `sessions.distilled_at TEXT`, `sessions.distilled_text TEXT`. Idempotent ALTER TABLE + `CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS sessions_starred`. `DERIVED_VERSION` stays at 6.
- **Wave 7.1a — Cluster P (partial): notifications + terminal + auto-title.** TODOs #92, #93, #171, #168.
  - **Web push notifications (#92).** VAPID keys lazy-generated on first `/api/notifications/push/vapid-public-key` request and stored in `~/.minder/vapid-keys.json`. Browser subscriptions stored in new `push_subscriptions` SQLite table. Settings → Notifications: permission button, subscribe/unsubscribe, per-device revoke, send-test-push button. 410 Gone responses automatically remove expired subscriptions. Dedup window: 5 minutes per channel+event+payload hash in `notification_log` table.
  - **Telegram notification bridge (#93).** Bot setup wizard in Settings → Integrations (bot token saved to `~/.minder/secrets.json`, chat ID in config). Plain-text messages truncated at 4000 chars. Test connection button. Dedup via shared `notification_log` table.
  - **Terminal launch (#171).** **Resume** button on session detail becomes a split button: primary "Open in terminal" spawns `claude --resume <id>` in the project's directory; dropdown secondary "Copy command" copies to clipboard. Cross-platform: `wt.exe`/`cmd.exe` on Windows, `osascript` (Terminal.app) on macOS, `gnome-terminal`/`konsole`/`xterm` on Linux. On spawn failure, toast shows the command with copy fallback. Settings → Terminal: platform-default display, binary override, test-launch button.
  - **LLM-powered session title generation (#168).** "Generate title" button on session detail calls the configured LLM endpoint (default: Anthropic Haiku 4.5) and stores a 4–8 word title in `sessions.generated_title`. "Regenerate" re-calls on demand. Sessions list prefers `generatedTitle` over raw first prompt when present. Settings → Auto-title: endpoint, model, API key (saved to `~/.minder/secrets.json`), test button.
  - **`manual-step-added` notification fan-out.** When a new `## ` entry is appended to any project's `MANUAL_STEPS.md`, the configured subset of `push` / `telegram` / `os` channels fires. Checkbox toggles do not fire. `os` channel handled browser-side in `NotificationListener`; `push` and `telegram` dispatched server-side from `manualStepsWatcher` via lazy-imported `dispatcher.ts`.
  - **Schema v7.** `sessions.generated_title TEXT`, new `push_subscriptions` table, new `notification_log` table. Automatic 30-day prune of `notification_log` on each server boot. `DERIVED_VERSION` stays at 6 (no JSONL re-derivation needed).

### Notes
- **TODO #40 (hook enable/disable) deferred.** No documented Claude Code mechanism for a `disabled: true` field on hook entries. The mechanism cited in the original plan originated in `chesketh/claude-config-manager` (third-party tool), not Claude Code itself. Verified against Claude Code hooks docs 2026-05-06. Defer until Claude Code adds the field, or until we ship a Project-Minder-owned UI-only filter (`.minder.json disabledHookKeys: string[]`) as a follow-up wave.

## [1.0.0] - 2026-05-03

> **Headline**: SQLite indexer goes default-on with a fully-indexed read path. Every JSONL-derived dashboard route (`/api/usage`, `/api/sessions{,/[id],/activity}`, `/api/agents{,/[id]}`, `/api/skills{,/[id]}`, `/api/stats`) now serves from `~/.minder/index.db` by default. Fall-throughs to file-parse stay only for v3-readiness windows and brand-new installs; silent error masking is gone.

### Changed
- **P2b-9 — silent fallback removed from the data façade.** Step 2 of the P2b-4 default-on rollout: when DB mode is requested and the DB is genuinely unhealthy (driver missing, schema init failed, connection null, or a SQL load throws), `src/lib/data/index.ts` now THROWS `DbUnavailableError` instead of swallowing the error and serving a file-parse result. Routes get a 500 — which is the right answer for "DB is supposed to work and doesn't." Pre-P2b-9 behavior masked failures via `logFallthroughOnce` and silently downgraded every read for the rest of the dev session, observed in soak as a single transient `EBUSY` poisoning the cached `ensureSchemaReady` (since fixed in P2c).
  - **`MINDER_USE_DB=0` still works** as the explicit file-parse opt-out — operators retain a documented escape hatch for debugging or platform-specific issues. The change only affects the "DB requested + DB broken" path.
  - **Two intentional fall-throughs preserved**, both logged as "expected during X" once per process per scope:
    1. **v3-readiness gate** (`needsReconcileAfterV3`): between migration apply and reconcile, `cost_usd` is 0 on every existing row. File-parse keeps numbers honest during the catch-up window. Without this, the SQL backend would silently serve `totalCost = $0`.
    2. **Empty-index gate** (sessions / agents / skills / claude usage): a brand-new install with the indexer still warming up returns zero rows; falling back keeps the dashboard populated rather than blank during the first scan. Per-session detail miss (session not in index yet) similarly falls back so a newly-arrived JSONL still resolves.
  - **`DbUnavailableError` exported** with a `reason: 'driver-missing' | 'init-failed' | 'connection-null' | 'load-failed'` discriminator and an optional `cause` chain back to the underlying error, so future route-level handling (typed retry, friendlier UI, etc.) can pattern-match without parsing a string. The default route handler doesn't distinguish — Next.js surfaces both as 500 — but the typed shape keeps the contract grep-able.
  - **Test-suite updates**: `tests/dataInitRetry.test.ts` first test flips from "fall-through to file" to "throws DbUnavailableError({reason: 'init-failed'})" while still pinning the retry-on-failure contract (second call must re-attempt `initDb()`). `tests/dataUsage.test.ts` "init-failure" test similarly flips to expect a throw. The other 642 tests are unaffected — the v3-catch-up fallthrough path keeps its existing fall-back behavior, so `tests/dataUsage.test.ts` "falls back when needs_reconcile_after_v3 is set" continues passing as-is. All 642 tests pass, typecheck clean.

### Fixed
- **P2c — three follow-ups from the P2b read-coverage arc.** Ship together as one slice so reviewers can land them in a single PR.
  - **`ensureSchemaReady` doesn't cache one-shot init failures** (`src/lib/data/index.ts`). Original behavior cached the `initDb()` Promise once per process; if the first call hit a transient `EBUSY` on the corruption-quarantine rename (observed in real soak), the cached `{available: false}` poisoned every DB-backed read until process restart, with `logFallthroughOnce` masking repeats. Now: only cache successful inits — clear the cached promise on failure (resolved or rejected) so the next caller retries. Concurrent in-flight callers still share one promise, so there's no thundering-herd risk during init itself; retries only kick in after a failed promise has settled. 2 new tests in `tests/dataInitRetry.test.ts` pin the contract (retry happens, in-flight sharing still works).
  - **`searchableText` restored in DB-backed `/api/sessions`** (`src/lib/data/sessionsListFromDb.ts`). Closes P2b-5 divergence #2 — `SessionsBrowser`'s content-search branch was a no-op under MINDER_USE_DB. New 6th query reads `(session_id, role, text_preview)` for non-empty previews in turn-order; `groupSearchable` builds the same shape as file-parse's `searchParts` accumulator (cap 4000 chars per session, assistant text sliced to 500 per turn, user text untruncated since ingest already capped `text_preview` at 500). Total payload for the typical 150-session corpus is a few MB. Help docs (`docs/help/sessions.md` + runtime copy) reverted to original wording — body-text search works under DB now. Small remaining quirk (file-parse iterates BLOCKS, DB iterates TURNS) covered by detail loader divergence #6; practical impact for content search is negligible.
  - **`sessions.status` populated at ingest** (`src/lib/db/ingest.ts` + `src/lib/data/sessionsListFromDb.ts`). Closes P2b-5 divergence #3 — `needs_attention` no longer silently absent under DB mode. Ingest now walks each parsed session inline with the same pending-pairs algorithm as `inferSessionStatus` (`src/lib/scanner/sessionStatus.ts`) and stores a snapshot in `sessions.status`. The full TypeScript `SessionStatus` (`working|idle|needs_attention`) doesn't fit the existing CHECK constraint and changing the constraint would require a SQLite table rebuild — not worth it for what's effectively a one-bit signal. Snapshot collapses to `'waiting'` (had unresolved pendings) vs `'inactive'` (no pendings). Loader applies time-gating against `file_mtime_ms` at READ time to derive `working / needs_attention / idle` — `working` if mtime fresh (< 90 s), `needs_attention` if in [90 s, 10 min] window, `idle` if older or stored=`'inactive'`. Sessions written before P2c (status=NULL) fall back to the original 2-min mtime heuristic until next full reconcile. **Documented staleness window**: `appendSessionTail` only refreshes status when the tail itself contains an assistant turn; user-only tails (e.g., a tool completion arriving alone) keep the prior `'waiting'` snapshot in place. Time-gating hides this for abandoned sessions (they age out to `idle` after 10 min) but a session that resolved its pendings within the same dev-server lifetime keeps showing as `working` / `needs_attention` until next full reconcile. Acceptable for the typical ~150-session corpus.

### Added
- **P2b-8 — SQL-backed `/api/stats` (Claude usage section).** Final slice in the P2b read-coverage arc: `/api/stats` no longer rehydrates the entire `~/.claude/projects` JSONL corpus on every dashboard load. New `loadClaudeUsageStatsFromDb` (`src/lib/data/claudeUsageFromDb.ts`) reads the `ClaudeUsageStats` shape (totalTokens, per-tool counts, models, cost, conversation count, error count) directly from indexed `sessions` / `turns` / `tool_uses` rows scoped by `project_dir_name IN (...)`. New `getClaudeUsage(projectPaths)` façade in `src/lib/data/index.ts` follows the established pattern: `MINDER_USE_DB` flag, v3 readiness gate, file-parse fall-through on driver-missing / init-failure / empty-result. The route's existing 10-min cache layered above is preserved; cache slot extended to carry the backend label so served-from-cache responses still report `X-Minder-Backend: db|file`.
  - **Variable-shape SQL** — the project-paths filter has variable cardinality, so the IN-list query is built with `db.prepare()` directly rather than `prepCached` (same caveat as `queryProjectDetails` in `usageFromDb.ts`). Per-prepare cost is absorbed by the route's 10-min cache. Three queries (totals scalar, tools GROUP BY, models DISTINCT) per refresh.
  - **`scanAllProjects()` stays file-backed** — it's the project-config scan, not JSONL-derived; out of scope for this slice. Only the JSONL-derived half migrates.
  - **Documented divergences from the file-parse path:** (1) `costEstimate` is **more accurate** under DB — file-parse buckets cache-only files as "unknown" → sonnet-fallback pricing (`scanConversationDirs` line ~801), while DB knows the actual model on every row via per-turn `applyPricing` at ingest. Treat as an improvement. `totalTokens` excludes cache tokens in both backends (matches `scanClaudeConversations:734`). (2) **Worktree sessions roll up to the parent project under DB.** Ingest applies `canonicalizeDirName` (`src/lib/usage/parser.ts:58`), which strips the `--<word>-worktrees-...` suffix from worktree dirs — so a session originating from `C--dev-my-app--claude-worktrees-foo` is stored with `project_dir_name = 'C--dev-my-app'`. File-parse uses raw dir names, so the worktree dir name isn't in `allowedDirs` when the caller passes the parent path, and worktree sessions are excluded entirely. Result: DB-backed totals for a parent project include its worktree work; file-backed totals don't. The DB behavior is arguably more useful, but it's a numeric difference reviewers should know about.
  - **ETag salt includes backend** — `stats-v2-${backend}` so a runtime backend swap (e.g. when the cached `ensureSchemaReady` flips after a DB hiccup recovery) rotates the ETag and clients re-fetch instead of being 304'd against bytes that may carry a different `costEstimate`. `maxMtimeMs` ETag input now flows from the façade's `meta.maxMtimeMs` (DB: `MAX(file_mtime_ms) FROM sessions`; file: `0`, with `result.scannedAt` carrying freshness on the file side) rather than the parser's `getJsonlMaxMtime()` (which stayed 0 in DB mode because nothing warmed the parser's FileCache).
  - **`encodePath` inlined** as a 3-character regex replace rather than imported from `claudeConversations.ts` — that module pulls in the full file-parse pipeline (pricing, fs caches, every scanner helper), and the read path shouldn't carry that weight at boot just to do a path-to-dirname encoding.
  - **4 new tests** in `tests/dataClaudeUsage.test.ts`: file backend default, fall-through on empty index, full backend-parity diff, empty-projectPaths cleanliness. Cost equality holds within `toBeCloseTo(4)` precision for the canonical-model fixture (the `costEstimate` divergence kicks in only for corpora with non-sonnet models on cache-hit files, which the fixture avoids). 640 tests pass, typecheck clean.
  - **End of arc.** P2b-5 through P2b-8 ship every JSONL-derived read path onto the SQLite index. The remaining file-parse callsites in the codebase are (a) the catalog walk (intentional — agents/skills/commands live as files), (b) `scanAllProjects` for project-config metadata (intentional — `.minder.json`, `package.json`, etc. aren't JSONL), and (c) the file-parse fallback paths inside the façade (kept for one release per the P2b-4 rollout plan; removal is the next slice once soak validates).

- **P2b-7 — SQL-backed `/api/skills` and `/api/skills/[id]`.** Mirror of P2b-6 against `tool_uses.skill_name`. New `loadSkillUsageFromDb` (`src/lib/data/skillsUsageFromDb.ts`) and `getSkillUsage()` façade in `src/lib/data/index.ts` use the same single-query / JS-fan-out shape, the same empty-rows fall-through, the same lazy-imported file-parse fallback, and the same route-cache-with-backend-label refactor. Index `tool_uses_by_skill` covers the WHERE clause.
  - **No documented divergences** vs the file-parse path. Both backends skip sidechain entries (`parser.ts:103` for file-parse, ingest skip for DB) and extract the skill name from the same `args.skill` field. `invocations`, `projects` map, `sessions[]` order, and `firstUsed` / `lastUsed` agree exactly when the indexer is up-to-date.
  - **4 new tests** in `tests/dataSkillsUsage.test.ts`: file backend default, fall-through on empty index, full backend-parity diff, empty-corpus cleanliness. 636 tests pass, typecheck clean.

- **P2b-6 — SQL-backed `/api/agents` and `/api/agents/[id]`.** New `loadAgentUsageFromDb` (`src/lib/data/agentsUsageFromDb.ts`) reconstructs the cross-project `AgentStats[]` shape from indexed `tool_uses` rows, replacing the `parseAllSessions` + `groupAgentCalls` rehydrate that previously fired on every catalog page load. Wired through a new `getAgentUsage()` façade in `src/lib/data/index.ts` that both routes consume; same `MINDER_USE_DB` flag, same file-parse fall-through on driver-missing / init-failure / empty-Agent-rows. Empty-rows is a fall-through (rather than an empty list) so a brand-new install with the indexer still warming up doesn't show "no agents used" when JSONL files exist. Response carries `X-Minder-Backend: db|file`.
  - **One query, JS fan-out** — `GROUP BY (agent_name, project_slug, session_id)` returns rows that fan out to all three AgentStats fields in a single pass: `invocations` sums per agent, `projects` sums per (agent, project), and `sessions[]` derives from the per-(agent, session) latest timestamp sorted DESC and capped at 50. Index `tool_uses_by_agent` covers the WHERE clause.
  - **No documented divergences** vs the file-parse path. Both backends skip sidechain entries (`parser.ts:103` for file-parse, ingest skip for DB) and extract the agent name from the same `args.subagent_type` field. `invocations`, `projects` map, `sessions[]` order, and `firstUsed` / `lastUsed` agree exactly when the indexer is up-to-date — verified by the new parity test.
  - **Façade ergonomics** — `getAgentUsage()` returns `{stats, meta}` with the same shape pattern as `getUsage` and `getSessionsList`. The catalog join in the routes (via `buildAgentAliasMap`) stays unchanged; only the rehydrate-then-aggregate half migrates. The `[id]` route's "load all stats then find by aliased entry" pattern is preserved because alias resolution requires the full stats list — and under DB mode the full list is now cheap (single GROUP BY) rather than a JSONL re-parse.
  - **Lazy-imports for the file-parse fallback** — `parseAllSessions` and `groupAgentCalls` are dynamic-imported inside `getAgentUsage`'s fallback branch so the DB happy path keeps the JSONL parser off the import graph entirely. Same posture as `loadUsageReportFromSql` already established for /api/usage.
  - **Route-cache shape extended** — `__agentsRouteCache` slots now carry `backend` alongside `data` and `cachedAt` so served-from-cache responses report the same `X-Minder-Backend` value the original computation produced. Without this, a cache hit would lose the backend signal.
  - **4 new tests** in `tests/dataAgentsUsage.test.ts`: file backend default, fall-through on empty index, full backend-parity diff (every numeric field + projects map + sessions ordering + firstUsed/lastUsed), empty-corpus cleanliness. 632 tests pass, typecheck clean.
  - **Soak observation** filed as a separate TODO: during P2b-6 verification, a transient `EBUSY` on the corruption-quarantine rename poisoned the data façade's cached `ensureSchemaReady()` for the rest of the dev session, silently downgrading every DB-backed route to file-parse. Two-fix proposal (retry-on-failure for the cache; retry-on-EBUSY for the rename) tracked in TODO.md.

- **P2b-5 — SQL-backed `/api/sessions` and `/api/sessions/activity`.** New `loadSessionsListFromDb` (`src/lib/data/sessionsListFromDb.ts`) reconstructs the cross-project `SessionSummary[]` shape from indexed `sessions / turns / tool_uses` rows instead of re-parsing every JSONL in `~/.claude/projects/` on every dashboard poll. Wired through a new `getSessionsList()` façade in `src/lib/data/index.ts` that both routes consume; same `MINDER_USE_DB` flag, same v3 readiness gate, same file-parse fall-through on driver-missing / init-failure / empty-index. Empty-index is treated as a fall-through (rather than an empty list) so a brand-new install with the indexer still warming up still surfaces sessions on the dashboard. Response carries `X-Minder-Backend: db|file`.
  - **Five queries per refresh** (one for the session headers, one each for per-session tool / skill / model breakdown maps), stitched in JS by `session_id`. `subagentCount` falls out of the tool-count query as `toolUsage['Agent']` — no separate query. Total wall-time on the user's real corpus (154 sessions): single-digit milliseconds vs the previous JSONL re-parse on every 30 s cache-miss.
  - **Documented divergences from the file-parse path** — same posture as `loadSessionDetailFromDb`: (1) `recaps` undefined (away_summary entries skipped at ingest); (2) `searchableText` undefined (not denormalized into the schema; **UI consequence**: `SessionsBrowser`'s content-search branch silently filters out everything for DB-backed sessions until a follow-up reconstructs it from `prompts_fts`); (3) `status` is heuristic-only (`working` if mtime < 2 min, `idle` otherwise — file-parse's `inferSessionStatus` can additionally return `needs_attention` for stale-with-pending-tools, which the DB path never emits); (4) sidechain entries skipped at ingest, so token sums / message counts / `toolUsage` / `subagentCount` / `costEstimate` for sessions that dispatched subagents are lower under DB; (5) `oneShotRate` derived from session-row `verified_task_count` / `one_shot_task_count` (pricing/classifier-version drift invisible until reconcile); (6) `costEstimate` reads pre-computed `sessions.cost_usd` (per-turn `applyPricing` at ingest); (7) `isActive` matches both backends; (8) `startTime` / `endTime` (and `durationMs`) derive from non-sidechain `turns.ts` rows under DB vs every JSONL entry's timestamp under file-parse — DB window strictly contained within file-parse window for sessions with sidechain or system entries before the first user turn or after the last assistant turn.
  - **Cache-shape unification** — both routes share `globalForSessions.__sessionsCache`; previously each declared a slightly different TS interface for the slot, which would have produced `NaN` ETag inputs if the activity route refreshed first. Both now use `{result: SessionsListResult, cachedAt, maxSessionMs}` so the cache is interoperable. The 30-s in-route cache stays — it avoids per-call assembly + serialization overhead during dashboard polling, even though the DB-backed loader is already cheap.
  - **No schema changes.** Existing indexes (`sessions_by_end_ts`, `tool_uses_by_skill`, `turns_by_role_ts`, plus PK prefixes) cover every aggregation. The detail loader's index work in P2b-3 already paid for this slice.
  - **4 new tests** in `tests/dataSessionsList.test.ts` mirroring `tests/dataSessionDetail.test.ts`: file backend default, fall-through on empty index, full backend-parity diff (every numeric field + sort order + project/model/tool/skill maps + divergence assertions), and empty-corpus cleanliness. Validated live: `curl http://localhost:4100/api/sessions` returns `X-Minder-Backend: db` with 154 sessions; activity endpoint returns 11 projects with 14-day buckets; project filter (`?project=dev-project-minder`) returns 24 correctly-filtered sessions. 628 tests pass, typecheck clean.
  - **Deferred** — `searchableText` reconstruction from `prompts_fts` (the data is in FTS5; a small JOIN at load time would restore content search under DB mode); ingest-side `inferSessionStatus` to populate `sessions.status` and close the heuristic divergence. Both queued as follow-ups; out of scope for this slice to keep the PR reviewable.

### Changed
- **P2b-4 — `MINDER_USE_DB` and `MINDER_INDEXER` default to on.** Both flags previously required an explicit `=1` to opt in to the SQLite-backed read path and the chokidar ingest watcher; with the data path's correctness validated through P2b-2 / P2b-3 / P2b-3.5 and the indexer's reconcile throughput tuned in the previous slice, the defaults flip. Read paths (`getUsage`, `getSessionDetail`) now consult `~/.minder/index.db` first; the in-process watcher starts at server boot. Set `MINDER_USE_DB=0` to force the legacy file-parse path, or `MINDER_INDEXER=0` to suppress the watcher (e.g. for benchmarking, or if the watcher misbehaves on a specific filesystem). `MINDER_INDEXER_WORKER` stays opt-in until worker mode is burned in.
  - **No fallback removal in this slice.** The DB path still falls back to file-parse on driver-missing / init-failure / v3-readiness-pending — the safety net stays in place for one release of soak time. A follow-up slice will remove the fallback once the new default has been validated in practice.
  - **Predicate inversion, not a flag rename.** `dbModeRequested()` now returns `process.env.MINDER_USE_DB !== "0"` (was `=== "1"`). The watcher's flag check inverts identically. Existing `MINDER_USE_DB=1` / `MINDER_INDEXER=1` settings keep working unchanged — the change is only visible to users who relied on the unset-default-off behavior.
  - **Test updates**: assertions that previously cleared the env var to land on the file-parse backend now set `=0` explicitly. New positive test (`tests/dataUsage.test.ts`) pins the inverted default — unset `MINDER_USE_DB` must produce `meta.backend === "db"`. `tests/dbIngestWatcher.test.ts` "returns idle status" test renamed and rewritten around `=0`.

### Fixed
- **Hydration error on dashboard** — `ProjectCard`'s CI-workflow badge was a `<Link>` nested inside the card's outer `<Link>`, producing invalid `<a>`-inside-`<a>` HTML and a Next.js hydration warning. The badge now renders as a `<span role="link">` that calls `router.push` on click and Enter/Space, matching the existing pattern used by the session-status and pin buttons. The outer card link still handles cmd/ctrl-click "open in new tab" for the project page.
- **Reconcile throughput: 88× speedup on schema-bump catch-up.** Profiled `reconcileSessionFile` against the user's real corpus (124k turns, 160 sessions) and found 99% of wall-time in the `DELETE FROM sessions` cascade, specifically the `turns_ad` AFTER DELETE trigger which filtered `prompts_fts` on UNINDEXED columns and scanned the entire FTS5 table per cascade-deleted turn — O(turns × fts_rows) per session-replace. A 366-turn session took 44 seconds in `write.delete` alone. Migration v4 drops the trigger; `writeSession` and the `reconcileAllSessions` prune loop now bulk-delete `prompts_fts` rows for the session in one scan before the cascade. Measured: 5.9 sessions/min → 519 sessions/min (~88×) on the same 10-session sample. The DERIVED_VERSION-bump catch-up that would have taken ~80–100 minutes now completes in ~20 seconds.
  - **Why not FTS5 external-content / rowid alignment** (the textbook fix): `turns` is `WITHOUT ROWID`, so `NEW.ROWID` is undefined and the rowid-aligned trigger can't be authored. Removing `WITHOUT ROWID` would require a full `turns` table rebuild — out of scope for a perf-fix slice. The bulk-pre-delete pattern delivers the measurable win without touching the storage layout.
  - **New contract**: any code path that deletes turns must clean `prompts_fts` for the affected session first. Today both write paths (`writeSession`, `reconcileAllSessions` prune loop) handle this. A new test in `tests/dbSchema.test.ts` pins the contract — direct `DELETE FROM turns` no longer auto-cleans the FTS index, so any future re-add of `turns_ad` is a deliberate decision rather than a regression.
  - **Optional ingest profiling hooks** added to `src/lib/db/ingest.ts` — `getIngestTimings()` / `resetIngestTimings()` plus a per-stage `tick()` gated on `MINDER_PROFILE_INGEST=1`. Zero overhead when disabled (single boolean check). Drives `scripts/profile-reconcile.mjs`, the per-stage profiler used to find this bottleneck. Kept for future ingest tuning passes.
  - **Test updates**: dbMigrations.test.ts version assertions bumped (3 → 4); dbSchema.test.ts FTS5 trigger test split into "INSERT/UPDATE in sync" (positive) and "DELETE doesn't auto-clean" (contract pin). All 623 tests pass.

### Added
- **P2b-3.5 — prepared-statement cache for read-side SQL paths.** New `prepCached(db, sql)` helper in `src/lib/db/connection.ts` memoizes `Statement` objects per literal SQL string against the singleton db handle. Refactored every read-side callsite in `src/lib/data/usageFromDb.ts` (16 prepares — totals, byModel, byProject, byCategory, daily, topTools, mcpStats, shellStats, oneShot, projectDetails, plus `getDbMaxMtimeMs` and `needsReconcileAfterV3`) and `src/lib/data/sessionDetailFromDb.ts` (3 prepares — sessions header, turns, tool_uses) to use the helper. Ingest is intentionally untouched — its prepares are loop-local within transactions and don't benefit from cross-request reuse.
  - **Lifecycle 1:1 with the db handle.** The cache lives on `ConnectionState` next to the db handle; `getDb()` creates a fresh `Map` on each successful open, `closeDb()` nulls it alongside `state.db`. No WeakMap, no cross-handle leakage, no chance of dangling Statements pinned to a closed Database under HMR cleanup.
  - **Foreign db handles bypass the cache.** `prepCached` checks `db === state.db` before consulting the cache; tests that construct their own `Database` (via `new Database(":memory:")`) get correct behavior without polluting the singleton's cache. Verified by a dedicated test case in `tests/preparedCache.test.ts`.
  - **Static-SQL contract.** The cache is unbounded by design (callsites are literal strings, ~17 distinct keys at steady state). `prepCached`'s docblock explicitly forbids dynamic/interpolated SQL — those callers (`/api/sql/route.ts`, which prepares user-supplied SQL) keep using `db.prepare()` directly.
  - **Measured win**: `/api/usage?period=all` warm went from 27–34 ms (P2b-2.5) to 18–24 ms (P2b-3.5) — ~30% faster, ~10 ms saved on a hot request. Theoretical estimate was 1–3 ms (17 prepares × 50–200 µs); the larger measured delta likely reflects skipped query-plan re-validation and reduced JS allocation pressure per request, not just the parse cost. Full methodology + before/after table in `docs/perf/baseline-2026-04.md` under "After P2b-3.5".
  - **4 new tests** in `tests/preparedCache.test.ts`: identity equality on same SQL, distinct Statements for different SQL, fresh cache after `closeDb()` + reopen, foreign-handle bypass. 622 of 623 tests pass (1 unrelated skip), typecheck clean.

- **P2b-3 — SQL-backed `/api/sessions/[sessionId]` detail loader.** New `loadSessionDetailFromDb` (`src/lib/data/sessionDetailFromDb.ts`) reconstructs the full `SessionDetail` shape from indexed `sessions / turns / tool_uses` rows instead of re-parsing the JSONL on every detail view. Wired through a new `getSessionDetail(sessionId)` façade in `src/lib/data/index.ts` behind the existing `MINDER_USE_DB=1` flag. Falls back to file-parse on any DB unavailability (driver missing, init failure, session not in index — covers the "session exists on disk but isn't indexed yet" edge cleanly).
  - **Three SELECTs per request** (`sessions` header, `turns`, and `tool_uses`), followed by single-pass aggregation in JS for `toolUsage`, `skillsUsed`, `subagents`, `fileOperations`, and the timeline. `modelsUsed` derived from the already-loaded `turns` rows — no separate `SELECT DISTINCT model` round-trip.
  - **Skills read from the indexed `tool_uses.skill_name` column** rather than re-parsing `arguments_json`. Same for `agent_name`. JSON parse only happens for the rows that need free-form fields (Bash command, Agent description fallback).
  - **`fileOperations` derived from `tool_uses` directly**, not `file_edits`, because the file-parse path emits one entry per tool_use (no dedup) while `file_edits` dedupes to one row per (session, turn, file) for hot-file analytics. Filtered to file-parse's exact tool set — Read/Write/Edit/Glob/Grep + Bash — so MultiEdit/NotebookEdit (which DO write to `file_edits`) are deliberately suppressed here for backend parity.
  - **Documented divergences from the file-parse path**, all surfaced in the loader's header comment: (1) `recaps` undefined (away_summary entries skipped at ingest); (2) `searchableText` undefined (not stored); (3) `subagents.messageCount` and per-agent `toolUsage` zeroed (sidechain entries skipped at ingest — type and description ARE preserved from `agent_name` + `arguments_json`); (4) `status` is a heuristic — `working` if `isActive`, `idle` otherwise; the DB path never emits `needs_attention`; (5) `bash` entries in `fileOperations` come from `tool_uses` (not `file_edits`, whose CHECK constraint excludes 'bash'); (6) **no `thinking` events and at most one `assistant` event per turn** — ingest doesn't persist content blocks, so multi-text-block / thinking timelines diverge from file-parse; (7) **sidechain entries skipped at ingest**, so `messageCount` / token totals / `costEstimate` can be lower than file-parse for sessions with subagents. SessionSummary aggregates and timeline content match file-parse within those bounds.
  - **Path-traversal hardening** preserved — same `^[a-f0-9-]+$` regex gate as `scanSessionDetail`, applied before the DB query so a malicious sessionId can't even hit prepared statements.
  - **Refactor**: extracted shared `getReadyDb()` helper in the façade. `tryDbBackend` (usage) and `tryDbSessionDetail` both apply the v3 readiness gate — session detail reads `sessions.cost_usd` (→ `costEstimate`) and `verified_task_count` / `one_shot_task_count` (→ `oneShotRate`), which are 0 on un-reconciled rows during the v3 catch-up window.
  - **4 new tests** in `tests/dataSessionDetail.test.ts`: file-parse default behavior, DB fallback when no row exists, full backend parity (every numeric field + timeline event-type sequence + fileOperations set + subagent type/description) modulo documented divergences, and path-traversal rejection. Response carries `X-Minder-Backend: db|file`. 618 of 619 tests pass (1 unrelated skip), typecheck clean.
  - **Deferred**: prepared-statement caching across requests is a broader perf change that should apply to every SQL read path uniformly (P2b-3.5 if/when measurement shows a per-request `prepare()` cost worth eliminating).

- **P2b-2.5 — SQL-aggregate read path for `/api/usage` (schema rollup).** The structural perf win the master plan budgeted: `/api/usage` no longer rehydrates turns into JS, it issues a handful of `SELECT SUM(...) GROUP BY ...` queries against indexed columns. Schema additions: `turns.cost_usd` (per-turn dollar cost stamped at ingest), `sessions.verified_task_count` + `sessions.one_shot_task_count` (precise one-shot numerator/denominator so `period=all` aggregates without rehydrate), and a new `category_costs(day, project_slug, category)` rollup table. `daily_costs` keeps its existing shape; this slice adds the category-keyed sister rollup.
  - **Migration v3** is additive ALTERs + `CREATE TABLE category_costs` (idempotent — fresh DBs already have the columns via `schema.sql` v1). `DERIVED_VERSION` bumped to 3 so existing turn rows re-parse on the next reconcile to populate the new columns. The migration sets `meta.needs_reconcile_after_v3 = '1'` as a readiness gate; the read-side façade falls back to file-parse while the flag is set so the SQL backend never returns `totalCost = $0` during the catch-up window. `reconcileAllSessions` clears the flag on success.
  - **Ingest changes**: `writeSession` and `appendSessionTail` now persist per-turn `cost_usd` and per-session `verified_task_count` / `one_shot_task_count`. `appendSessionTail` reads `cost_usd` directly from `SUM(turns.cost_usd)` instead of running a second JS pricing pass. New `refreshCategoryCosts(db, tuples)` mirrors `refreshDailyCosts` shape but is pure SQL (no JS pricing pass — turn-level cost is already stamped). `reconcileSessionFile` returns `affectedCategoryTuples` alongside `affectedDays`; `reconcileAllSessions` batches both for end-of-pass refresh and unions OLD + NEW (day, project, category) tuples on full-replace via `collectExistingCategoryTuples` so a classifier-version bump that moves a turn between categories doesn't leave a stale rollup row.
  - **Read-side rewrite**: `loadFilteredUsageTurns` (rehydrate-then-aggregate) replaced with `loadUsageReportFromSql` (`src/lib/data/usageFromDb.ts`) — direct SQL aggregates for totals, byModel, byProject, byCategory, daily, topTools, mcpStats, oneShot, and projectDetails. shellStats stays JS-side because binary tokenization (`extractBinary`) lives in JS, but only Bash / PowerShell rows in the period are pulled — a tiny fraction of `tool_uses`. `byCategory.oneShotRate` is intentionally omitted in the SQL path (computing it would require a per-(category, session) one-shot pre-aggregate; out of scope).
  - **Two known divergences from file-parse**, both intentional and documented in `usageFromDb.ts`: (1) `byCategory.oneShotRate` undefined in SQL path; (2) `oneShot` for bounded periods over-counts boundary sessions slightly (period=all has zero divergence, which is the case the master plan's perf claim covers).
  - **Tests**: `dataUsage.test.ts` parity expanded to cover daily / topTools / mcpStats / shellStats / oneShot dimensions per-key (was only project / model / category / tool names). New `dbMigrations.test.ts` test simulates a v2 DB upgrading to v3 and verifies columns added, table created, readiness flag set, only v3 in `appliedMigrations`. New `dataUsage.test.ts` test simulates the readiness flag re-set and verifies file-parse fallback.
  - **Validated**: 614 tests pass, typecheck clean. Cold/warm `time curl '/api/usage?period=all'` against the user's real DB to be captured in the perf baseline doc.
  - **Deferred to P2b-2.6**: `queryByModel` / `queryByProject` / `queryDaily` / `queryTotals` still aggregate from raw `turns ⨝ sessions` rather than reading the existing `daily_costs` rollup. Wires up the structural rewrite cleanly for review; the rollup-driven path is a follow-up if real-DB perf measurement on `/api/usage?period=all` doesn't hit the 50–200 ms target.

- **P2b-2 — read-side data façade with `MINDER_USE_DB=1` flag.** New `src/lib/data/index.ts` houses `getUsage(period, project)` with two interchangeable backends behind one signature. Default remains the file-parse path (`parseAllSessions` + JSONL FileCache); setting `MINDER_USE_DB=1` switches to a SQLite-backed path that loads filtered turns + tool_uses directly from `~/.minder/index.db` and runs the **same** `aggregateUsage()` logic over them. Truncation parity is verified: `parser.ts` already truncates `extractText` to 500 chars and `extractToolResults` to 2000 chars, identical to the indexer's `text_preview` / `tool_result_preview` columns — so `classifyTurn` and `detectOneShot` consume byte-identical inputs across backends. Falls through to file-parse on any DB failure (driver missing, init failure, getDb null) so a misconfigured indexer never breaks `/api/usage`. The fall-through is logged once per process. Response carries `X-Minder-Backend: db|file`. ETag derives from `getJsonlMaxMtime()` for the file backend and `MAX(file_mtime_ms) FROM sessions` for the DB backend; both invalidate when JSONL rotates or grows because the indexer's `appendSessionTail` updates `file_mtime_ms` on every tail.
  - **Honest scope**: this slice's win is "skip the 1.1 GB JSONL re-parse on cold cache" — turns rehydrate into the existing aggregator rather than running SQL aggregates directly. The structural perf win (`SUM(...) GROUP BY` per dimension) needs schema additions (`turns.cost_usd` and a `category_costs` rollup) that ship as P2b-2.5. Document the staged rollout so we don't claim a perf number we haven't earned yet.
  - **Aggregator refactor**: extracted `aggregateUsage(turns, period)` from `generateUsageReport(period, project)` so the DB backend can pass pre-loaded turns directly. The existing public signature is preserved — `generateUsageReport` is now a thin wrapper that loads via `parseAllSessions` then calls the new aggregator.
  - **3 new tests** in `tests/dataUsage.test.ts`: file backend default, full backend-parity diff (totalCost, byProject, byModel, byCategory, topTools), and fall-through to file when `initDb` fails. The parity test runs the same fixture through both backends in one `it()` and asserts the reports agree on every dimension that doesn't depend on wall-clock.
  - **Validated**: 612 of 613 tests pass (1 unrelated skip), typecheck clean.

- **P2b-1 — read-only SQL endpoint.** `GET /api/sql?sql=…` and `POST /api/sql {sql, params?}` against the local SQLite index at `~/.minder/index.db`. SELECT-only with two-layer enforcement: a regex pre-gate rejects non-SELECT/WITH leading keywords (catches the obvious `DELETE`, `DROP`, `CREATE`, `ATTACH`, `PRAGMA`, `VACUUM`, `INSERT`, `UPDATE`, etc.), and `stmt.readonly` (better-sqlite3's compiled-statement introspection) is the authoritative check that catches the weird cases. Result rows iterate with a hard cap of 10 000; queries past the cap return `truncated: true` instead of erroring. POST accepts both positional `params: ["x"]` and named `params: {key: "x"}` for safe binding. Distinct failure modes: 400 for bad SQL or disallowed statements, 503 for `db unavailable` (driver missing OR schema not yet initialized) so the UI can show "indexer hasn't run yet" vs "your query is wrong." No auth on the route — local-only dashboard convention. Validated against the user's real 231 MB DB: `SELECT COUNT(*) FROM sessions` returns in 1 ms, top-projects aggregation across 158 sessions in 1 ms.
  - **Schema-readiness gate.** Route calls `initDb()` (idempotent; cached per process) on first request. Without this, a cold start with no `~/.minder/index.db` would auto-create an empty file via `getDb()` and queries against `sessions` etc. would fall into the 400 "no such table" path instead of the documented 503. Cached as a promise so concurrent first requests share one in-flight init rather than racing migrations.
  - **14 new tests** in `tests/apiSql.test.ts`: COUNT against populated DB, regex layer rejection, DROP/CREATE/ATTACH/PRAGMA/INSERT/UPDATE/VACUUM all 400, CTEs accepted (`WITH … SELECT`), malformed SQL surfaces SQLite's own `no such table` message, 10 000-row clamp via recursive CTE that produces 10 001 rows, POST + positional params, POST + named params, missing-sql 400, malformed-JSON 400, params-not-array-or-plain-object 400, driver-missing 503, auto-init on cold start (no prior `initDb`), and 503 when `initDb` reports the schema is unavailable.
  - Branch / route file is purely additive — no existing behavior changes. P2b-2 will start moving primary read paths onto the index behind a `MINDER_USE_DB=1` flag; this slice exists first so debugging tools land before the migrations they're meant to debug.

### Performance
- **P2a slice 2.4 phase 2 — real watcher inside the worker.** Builds on phase 1 (the `worker_threads` host scaffolding). The chokidar-based ingest watcher now runs inside the worker process when `MINDER_INDEXER_WORKER=1`, with the main thread serving HTTP requests immediately while the initial reconcile of `~/.claude/projects` (3k+ JSONL files, 30+ s on first boot) happens in the background. Cold-boot UX validated in production: HTTP 200 from `/api/projects` in ~3.4 s, instrumentation log fires `[ingest-worker] spawned` instantly. `MINDER_INDEXER=1` (in-process watcher) remains the default and the fallback path; phase 2 is strictly opt-in until we've burned in worker mode.
  - **`scripts/build-worker.mjs`** — esbuild bundle of `src/lib/db/ingestWatcher.ts` into `workers/dist/ingestWorker.mjs` (single ESM file, ~58 KB, ~50 ms build). Wired into `predev` and `prebuild` so the bundle is always fresh before Next.js starts. `better-sqlite3` and `chokidar` stay external (the worker resolves them from `node_modules` at runtime, same as the main thread). `server-only` is aliased to a no-op stub at bundle time (the package's runtime throw is a Next.js client-boundary check, irrelevant in a Node worker thread). Banner injects `createRequire` / `__dirname` / `__filename` shims so CJS-style code in the dependency graph (notably `migrations.ts`'s `__dirname`-relative schema lookup and `connection.ts`'s dynamic `require("better-sqlite3")`) keeps working in the ESM bundle.
  - **`workers/ingestWorker.mjs`** — phase-2 entry point: dynamic-imports `./dist/ingestWorker.mjs`, exposes a small message protocol (`start` / `stop` / `status` / `ping`), drives `startIngestWatcher` / `stopIngestWatcher` / `getWatcherStatus` from the bundle. Reports `started` / `error/phase=start` / `stopping` back to the host.
  - **`workerHost.ts`** — new `awaitStart` option (default true for tests; instrumentation passes `false` so a slow initial reconcile doesn't block server startup), new `sendStart` / `watcherOptions` / `startTimeoutMs` for the start handshake. The fire-and-forget path catches handshake failures and surfaces them via `console.warn` rather than swallowing.
  - **`instrumentation.ts`** — passes `awaitStart: false` so `register()` returns as soon as the worker is alive and the watcher module is loaded. The watcher's initial reconcile runs in the background; HTTP requests are served while it completes.
  - **Phase-2 test** in `tests/dbWorkerHostPhase2.test.ts`: spawns the real bundled worker against a tmpdir projects root, asserts `running: true`, stops cleanly. Skipped when `better-sqlite3` / `chokidar` aren't loadable. Builds the bundle on-demand if `workers/dist/` is empty (CI normally hits this path via `prebuild`).
  - **Validated in production**: `next build && MINDER_INDEXER_WORKER=1 npx next start -p 4199` on Windows. `[ingest-worker] spawned` log fires immediately, `/api/projects` returns HTTP 200 in 3.4 s. (The 30 s chokidar `ready` timeout for the user's real `~/.claude/projects` falls back to sweep-only mode — pre-existing watcher behavior on huge directories, not phase-2 specific.)
  - **Deps**: `esbuild` added as devDep. `server-only` not added — Next.js's main-thread resolution doesn't require it installed, and the worker bundle inlines a no-op stub.
- **P2a slice 2.4 phase 1 — worker_threads host scaffolding.** Introduces a Node `worker_threads` host (`src/lib/db/workerHost.ts`) plus a trivial ping/pong worker entry (`workers/ingestWorker.mjs`) so we can validate the spawn / ready / message / terminate / crash-respawn lifecycle in the Next.js + Turbopack environment before moving the real chokidar watcher in. Phase 2 will replace the trivial worker handler with one that drives `startIngestWatcher` (loader strategy decided once we see a real TS-import failure inside the worker).
  - **New env flag `MINDER_INDEXER_WORKER=1`** gates the worker path. `MINDER_INDEXER=1` continues to start the in-process watcher unchanged — it remains the default and acts as a fallback if the worker path turns out to be broken on a given platform / Next.js version. If `MINDER_INDEXER_WORKER=1` is set but the worker fails to spawn, instrumentation falls through to the in-process path so users always have working ingest.
  - **`workers/ingestWorker.mjs` lives at the project root** (not under `src/`) so Next.js / Turbopack don't try to bundle it. Plain `.mjs` ESM that Node loads directly via `new Worker()`. Path resolved via `process.cwd()` to avoid the dev-vs-`.next/` divergence and `import.meta.url` portability mess.
  - **`workerHost` lifecycle contract**: idempotent `startWorker()` (second call replaces prior worker), graceful `stopWorker()` (sends `stop` then `terminate()`, also clears any pending ready-timeout and rejects a pending `readyPromise` so a stop-during-startup unblocks the awaiting caller immediately), `getWorkerStatus()` snapshot, `postMessage` / `onWorkerMessage` for subscribers, configurable ready timeout (default 10 s; tests use 500 ms) that force-terminates a stalled worker, and crash-respawn with exponential backoff (500 ms → 2 s → 10 s) capped at 5 unexpected crashes per hour before giving up.
  - **Subscriber registry on host state, not on the Worker instance.** `onWorkerMessage` adds the handler to a `Set<MessageSubscriber>` that survives crash-respawn — the new worker's internal listener fans out to existing subscribers without any re-subscribe step. (Prior shape attached the listener directly to the Worker instance, so unsubscribing after a respawn targeted the wrong worker.)
  - **8 new tests** in `tests/dbWorkerHost.test.ts` covering: spawn → ready → running, ping/pong round-trip, idempotent stop, idempotent start (replaces prior worker), respawn after a synthetic crash, subscription survival across crash-respawn, rejection on the ready timeout path, and `stopWorker` rejecting a pending `readyPromise` (proves stop-during-startup unblocks in < 2 s instead of waiting the full timeout). Tests materialise inline `.mjs` workers into tmpdir so they don't depend on `process.cwd()` resolution under vitest.
  - **Validated in production** — `next build && MINDER_INDEXER_WORKER=1 next start` on Windows logs `[ingest-worker] started; entry=...\workers\ingestWorker.mjs` and serves `/api/projects` HTTP 200 while the worker is alive. `next dev` validation requires the user to restart their existing dev server with the flag set; the production path is the stronger evidence anyway because it's what the deploy path exercises.
- **P2a slice 2.3 — byte_offset incremental tail.** A session JSONL that grows (the common case while an agent is working) now reconciles by reading only the new bytes instead of re-parsing the whole file. Existing turn / tool_use / file_edit rows stay put — the tail just appends new ones starting at `MAX(turn_index) + 1` and the session row's aggregates re-derive from the union of old + new turns. On a 50 MB session-in-progress that adds one turn, reconcile work drops from 50 MB → ~1 KB of read.
  - **`reconcileSessionFile` dispatch** — three branches now: (1) gate (file unchanged → 0); (2) tail (same path, derived_version match, size grew, mtime forward → tail-append); (3) full replace (any other change, including file rename, version bump, file shrink, or first-time ingest).
  - **`readJsonlSession` parameterized with `{ fromOffset, startTurnIndex }`** — when `fromOffset > 0`, reads from the position immediately after the last consumed `\n` (the invariant carried by `sessions.byte_offset` since P2a-2.1) and assigns turn indexes starting from `startTurnIndex` so they don't collide with existing rows.
  - **`appendSessionTail`** — INSERTs new rows then UPDATEs the session row's aggregates from old + new combined. Numeric aggregates (token totals, turn counts, error counts, start/end timestamps) re-derive directly in SQL via `SUM` / `MIN` / `MAX` on the turns table. `primary_model` is one indexed `GROUP BY` query. `has_one_shot` re-runs `detectOneShot` over the full UsageTurn[] (rehydrated from DB rows via the new `loadExistingTurnsAsUsage` helper) because the detector's verdict on a prior turn can flip when a verification turn lands in the tail.
  - **Schema migration v2** adds `turns.tool_result_preview` so the rehydration of user-with-tool-result turns survives a tail-append round-trip. Without it, `detectOneShot`'s error-pattern check (`FAIL`, `Error:`, etc.) saw `undefined` for prior failed verifications, and `has_one_shot` could flip to true on a sequence that had actually failed. `DERIVED_VERSION` bumped to 2 so existing rows re-parse on first reconcile after upgrade and the column is populated before any tail relies on it. v2 migration is idempotent — fresh DBs run the latest `schema.sql` (column already present) and skip the `ALTER TABLE` via a `PRAGMA table_info` check.
  - **Ranged tail read** uses `createReadStream({ start })` instead of `fs.readFile + Buffer.subarray`. The OS only delivers bytes after the offset; an active 50 MB session log now costs ~1 KB of read per appended turn instead of re-reading the whole prefix.
  - **`last_prompt` fallback fixed** — when a tail contains no new human prompt, we keep the existing `last_prompt` instead of regressing it to `initial_prompt`.
  - **Mid-flush safety: `byte_offset` never advances past a partial line.** Both full-parse and tail-parse paths now read up to the LAST `\n` byte and park the cursor there. Anything after the last newline is treated as a partial line that hasn't been flushed yet — the next reconcile picks it up once the writer finishes. Without this, a watcher firing on a half-written line would silently drop that turn forever.
  - **Truncated `arguments_json` recovery on rehydrate.** Bumped `ARGS_JSON_LIMIT` from 10 KB to 32 KB and added a best-effort `command` extraction in `parseStoredArgs`. When stored args exceed the cap and `JSON.parse` fails, a regex match recovers just the `command` field so `detectOneShot` can still see Bash / PowerShell verification commands across tail-appends.
  - **7 new tests**: tail-append preserves existing turn_indexes; file shrink falls back to full replace with cascade cleanup; `has_one_shot` flips from 0 → 1 when an Edit turn is followed by a tail-appended Bash(test) + successful result; tail rehydration preserves `toolResultText` so a previously-FAILED verification correctly excludes itself from one-shot counting; v2 migration is idempotent on a v1 DB whose column was dropped; `byte_offset` parks at the last `\n` and a previously-partial line is recovered once flushed; truncated Bash command JSON still surfaces `command` to `detectOneShot` after a tail.
- **P2a slice 2.2 — chokidar watcher + `MINDER_INDEXER` flag.** The ingest pipeline now self-runs at server startup behind an env flag. With `MINDER_INDEXER=1` set, Next.js's `instrumentation.ts` hook calls `startIngestWatcher()` once per server process: initial reconcile + chokidar watch on `~/.claude/projects/**/*.jsonl` + 30 s mtime-sweep belt-and-braces for cases where filesystem events are silently dropped (WSL, network shares). Without the flag set, this is a strict no-op; the dashboard continues on the file-parse path.
  - **`src/lib/db/ingestWatcher.ts`** — `startIngestWatcher(opts)`, `stopIngestWatcher()`, `getWatcherStatus()`. globalThis singleton survives HMR (a second `start` call closes the prior watcher first). Per-file 250 ms debounce coalesces a fast burst of `change` events on an active session JSONL. Single-flight gate — if a change fires while a reconcile is mid-flight, it's queued for after completion rather than racing on the writer transaction. `awaitWriteFinish` set to 250 ms in production so we never parse a half-flushed line; tests pass shorter overrides for speed. chokidar imports lazily; if the module fails to load (uncommon platform), the watcher falls back to sweep-only mode.
  - **`instrumentation.ts`** at repo root — Next.js's official server-startup hook. Gated on `process.env.NEXT_RUNTIME === "nodejs"` and `process.env.MINDER_INDEXER === "1"`; logs the initial reconcile time on success or a warning on failure. Hard-coded to skip in test environments via the watcher's own `NODE_ENV !== "test"` guard so vitest never spawns a stray watcher against real `~/.claude/projects/`.
  - **4 new tests** in `tests/dbIngestWatcher.test.ts`: idle status when flag is unset, initial reconcile populates a pre-existing session, ingestion of a session created after the watcher starts (waits on chokidar's `ready` event before file creation to avoid the `ignoreInitial: true` race), and idempotent `stop()`. Tests pass `bypassEnvFlag: true` so they don't have to mutate the env, and `usePolling: true` so chokidar is reliable inside Windows tmpdirs.
- **P2a slice 2.1 — session ingest pipeline (in-process).** Reads `~/.claude/projects/**/*.jsonl` and populates `sessions`, `turns`, `tool_uses`, `file_edits`, plus the `daily_costs` rollup.
